After I have completed this book for you, O Sons, which is the last of medical science with its completion and I have finished it in its entirety, after its expositions and its declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this Tractate which is part of the operation, that is, surgery with the hand.
Because surgery with the hand is in our region and time completely absent, until perhaps the knowledge of it perished, and its trace was cut off: and there remained from it, except for small descriptions in books of ancients, which were altered by hands: and errors and hesitation happened to them, until their intentions were closed, and the power of him was extended: It seemed to me, that I should revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise in it according to the way of exposition, and declaration, and abbreviation: and that I should come with the forms of instruments cautery, and the rest of the instruments of work: when it is done from the addition of declaration, and from the preparation of it which is necessary.
The cause why a good artificer is not found in our time with his own hand is: because the art of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to exercise himself before that in the knowledge of anatomy, which Galen narrated, until he knows the attachments of the members, and their forms, and their conjunctions, and separations, and has knowledge of bones, and nerves, and tendons, and their number, and their exits, and the pulsations of veins, both quiet and moving, and the places of their exit.
And because of this Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with work little, especially in the art of the hand.
We have now spoken of that at the beginning of this book.
For whoever is not learned in what we have said about anatomy, he will not be able to purge himself, but rather fall into error, by which men are slain: just as I have seen many of those who form themselves from this knowledge, and boast of it without knowledge, and without experience.
That is, because I saw a foolish physician follow an abscess on the neck of a woman, and he cut into some arteries in her neck; therefore, blood flowed from the woman until she died between his hands.
And I saw another physician who dared to extract a stone from a man who had advanced in age, and the stone was large. Therefore it came to him, and he extracted it with the fragment of the bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And I indeed had been called to remove it; and I saw from the size of the stone, and the disposition of the patient, that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was receiving a stipend from a certain Duke in our land for medicine: and it happened to an eunuch, black, who was with him, a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the physician hastened with his ignorance, and bound the fracture above the wound with splints, and nails, with a strong bandage, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he completed it according to his desires. Afterwards he dismissed him for some days, and ordered him not to loosen the ligature. And he stood thus until the abscess came to his leg, and his foot, and it came to ruin.
I was therefore summoned to him: and I hurried to loosen the ligament: and tranquility followed, and he was freed from his pains.
Nevertheless, corruption was already confirmed in the limb: and I could not restrain it.
Therefore when corruption has ceased to wander through the limb until it has perished.
And I saw another physician who lanced a cancerous abscess: and it was ulcerated after days, until the malignancy of it had increased with its lord.
That is, because when it is a pure cancer from the humor of melancholy, then it is not necessary that it come to it with iron at all, unless it is in a limb which can bear to have the whole thing cut off.
And therefore, sons, it is necessary for you to know that surgery with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, surgery which is accompanied by health; and surgery, with which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have now aroused in every place of this book, where there is an operation, a terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you, that you avoid it, and halve it: that they may not find a foolish way to speak, and to dishonor.
Therefore, take the measure with care and protection, and your patients with ease and firmness, and use the best way leading by the grace of God to salvation and a praiseworthy succession: and dismiss terrible illnesses difficult to heal: and remove your souls from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation may enter upon you in your faith and your well-being.
For it is more enduring for your glory, and more sublime in this world, and finally to your quantities.
For Galen indeed said in some of his precepts. Do not treat a bad ailment: so that you are not called a bad physician.
Now however this treatise is divided into three chapters.
First Chapter.
Of cautery with fire, and cautery with sharp medicine, a chapter, and ordered from the head to the feet, and the shapes of instruments, and cautery tools: and all that is necessary in the operation.
Chapter Two.
Of incision and piercing, bloodletting and punction, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things to these: and the whole chapter, arranged according to the forms of instruments.
Chapter Three.
On restoration, and dislocation, and healing of torsion, and similar things:  a chapter arranged from head to foot, and the shapes of instruments.
But before we remember the operation with him, it is necessary that I say the quality of his aids, and his harms: and in what complexion he is shown.
Therefore I say that discourse on the quality of cautery and its use is a lengthy and subtle science, and a hidden secret.
Even many wise men spoke on this subject and disagreed about it; and for my part, I find it enough from their words, fearing an extension.
Therefore, I say that cauterization is effective universally for every condition, which is with matter and without matter, except for two conditions, which are hot condition without matter and dry condition without matter.
When the complexion was warm and moist they separated with the material. Some have said that a cautery is helpful in this. And others said the opposite of this, namely that cauterization is not suitable in illness which is from heat and dryness; because nature is heat, and it is unsuitable that it be healed from hot and dry disease with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite of this said: that by cauterization healing is done in every ailment hot and dry that happens in the bodies of humans: because when you compare the body of a human and its humidities to the complexion of fire, you find the body of a human cold.
And I indeed say by his saying: because from experience already it has shown itself to me many times.
Nevertheless, it ought not to come to pass that one should undertake this, unless he has already been tested and trained in the last exercise of the chapter on Cauterization, and has recognized the diversity of human complexions, and the disposition of illnesses in themselves, and their causes, and accidents, and the space of time for them.
Of the remaining complexions there is no fear: and especially in cold and moist ailments. For now all physicians have come together on these matters; and they did not disagree concerning the help of cautery in them.
And know, sons, that from the secret of healing by cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine is this: because fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the member that is cauterized; and it does not harm another member joined with it, except with little harm.
The action of burning in medicine comes to that which lengthens from the limbs; and perhaps it causes pain in the limb to occur that is difficult to heal, and perhaps it kills.
Fire, however, because of its subtlety and goodness of substance, does not do this unless it is excessive.
Now indeed it has been made known to us by experience, because of the length of service and study with the art, and standing over the truth of things: and for this I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not so, because it is not permitted to me in this book of mine, to bring to you the hidden secret by fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies of its expulsion, which expels diseases with a philosophical demonstrative discourse, that would agree with your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree about the time in which cautery should be done, and put forward a better time for truth.
And I say that cauterization is fitting at all times; for the harm arising from time is submerged in the benefit which is drawn with cauterization. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary pains, strong and urgent, which do not tolerate delay; because it is feared from them that an evil may happen which is greater than a small harm caused by the time passing.
And do not let it enter your minds, O sons, that which is not feared by the vulgar and foolish physicians, namely that in illnesses that are healed by cauterization, there is not always a return; and they put forth this as a consequence, and the matter is not as they think: because cauterization is not otherwise than medicine, which alters complexion, and dries up the humidities which are the causes, wherefore pains occur.
However, cauterization is superfluous over medicine because of the speed of its health and the power of its operation, and the intensity of its dominion: and it is possible that illness may return after some time according to the constitution of the sick person, and the location of his illness, and the virtue of him, and what is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in him, and what comes to him in its acquisition from foods, and similar things from causes, unless illness occurs in which cauterization is administered.
Pain that is slight in a limb due to few excesses and moistures, such as the pain of a tooth, because of the pain, and similar to it, for it is possible that the pain does not return there. But that is done in few cases.
But the common saying that cautery is the last resort of medicine is a true saying: not for what they intend by it; because they believe that it is not a cure that compares with medicine, nor with anything else after the occasion of cautery.
The matter is contrary to this, and the intention, that cautery is the last of medicine, is not so, except when we administer modes of treatment in some illnesses, and those medicines do not help; then, at the end of the matter, we administer cautery, and it helps: therefore, it falls that cautery is the last of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that a cautery with gold is better than a cautery with iron: and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold, and the sublimity of its substance: and they said that it does not make pus the place of cauterization. But that is not absolutely true; for I have already proven it, and found that it does not do that in some bodies without others.
And a cautery with itself is good, and better than with iron, as they have said. However, when you heat the cautery with fire from gold, it is not clear to you when it is heating according to the quantity that you want, because of the redness of the gold: and when it approaches to it coldness, and if you add fire above it, it melts in the fire, and turns into sheets.
Therefore the artificer comes from that into employment: and for this reason cautery is made with iron among us more quickly and nearer, from rightness to operation.
And I indeed have arranged this Chapter on Cauterization, according to chapters; and I have arranged them from head to foot: so that they may help the one who seeks what he wants from it.
Chapter II.
This applies cauterization to the domain of moisture and coldness over the brain: which two are causes of inflammation, and multiplicity of flow of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and multiplicity of sleep, and toothache, and sore throat: and universally all illness, which happens from coldness, such as paralysis, and inflammation, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you should instruct the sick person: that first it be evacuated with a medicinal solution cleansing the head for three nights, or four, according to what the strength of the infirm and his age and his habit require.
Then command him to make his head shave with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands square, so that he has now placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his eyes. Whenever therefore your middle finger shall have passed over it, mark that place with an unbleached one.
Then cautery with olive oil fire: this is its form.
Then place it on the marked spot with the unfastened, descending part so that your hand may be gradually tightened, and you turn it. Then lift your hand quickly, and look at the place.
If you see already exposed from the bone the quantity of alkiel, or the quantity of zeuherbi, then elevate your hand. And if not, repeat your hand with the iron itself, or with another from itself if it becomes cold: until the bones which I told you appear.
Then take some salt, and dissolve it in water, and drink it into the wound, and put it over the place: and leave it for three days.
Then place upon it a cloth soaked in butter, and let it remain over the site until the fire's scurf is destroyed. Then treat it with ointment of four drugs, until it is healed.
They have said that the more a wound remains open, the more it emits pus, and therefore it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone; and the cautery should be held until something of the thickness of bone is burned away.
Then it is scraped after that which has been burned from bone, then it is cared for.
And others say that it is necessary that with the cauterizing iron one should arrive at the utmost, until it impresses into the bone a form, so that the bone falls off, which happens as in the shape of a chisel; or an instrument which women put on the small alphabet infusion; and they believe that vapors of the head are exhaled from this place, and the wound be left open for a long time.
Then it is cared for until it consolidates.
To me, these two kinds of cautery do not appear at all except in certain people according to the way of fear.
And to dismiss him, in my opinion, is better for his health.
The head is weakened by the disruption of its natural continuity, as we have demonstrated in the other limbs: and especially when the body of a weak patient is naturally debilitated. And indeed the first kind of cauterization is safer and better for me, and I use it; therefore operate with it in safety.
Chapter III.
When a chronic pain occurs throughout the whole head: and it continues in the sick person, and he uses pig fat, and ointments, and head purges, and oils, and emplastrum. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, which we have described, and it does not help anything from those: then consider. If the head of the sick person is strong by nature's creation and not weak, and it finds intense cold, then cauterize with a cautery beneath it a little. Then cauterize it on every horn of his head with a cautery, so that it does not penetrate the skin, and uncover from bone the quantity which we have narrated. And cauterize him with one cautery on the back of his head, in the place which is called "was": and it is a place where a ventouse is placed; and elevate your mattress here, and do not uncover the bone. For he found himself in pain because of this, and it was different from the pain of other cautery burns on all parts of the head.
And I shall say this regarding the cautery: and it ought to be a cautery for cauterizing the horns of the head, and the nape of its neck with a finer cautery than that used for cauterizing the middle of the head.
Chapter IV.
When there is pain and swelling in the head, or pain extends to the eye, and the head is cleansed with purifying medicines, and the rest of the treatment, which I have said in the divisions of diseases, is administered, and this does not benefit at all; then cauterization is done in it according to two modes: either cauterization with a burning sharp medicine; or with iron.
A cautery with a sharp and burning medicine is, to take one tooth of another, and to scrape it, and to cut off the extremities of it from both sides. Then cut a place of pain in time with a wide lancet, until a place is made under the skin, in which the tooth is caught.
Therefore introduce it into the very skin, until it is covered; then bind over it with a little poultice of a decent constriction, and let it be for fifteen hours; then unbind it, and remove the one, and leave the wound for two or three days: afterwards put upon it a pad immersed in butter, until a place produces pus; then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish to do this with certain medicines that burn, which I have written about in the twelfth treatise, on Burning Medicines.
Cauterization of it with iron, is according to this manner. Burning cautery, whose form is this.
And it is called Claulis: because the shape of its head is like the shape of a key, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle of it is a small eminence.
Then place it over the spot and hold your hand: and you revolve the iron gradually with speed: and let the quantity which is burned be as the thickness of the skin. And lift up your hand so that the artery below is not burned and blood does not flow.
Then soak a cloth in salt water, and place it over the location, and leave it for three days; then put the cloth with butter on top: afterwards, care for it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this headache with the second end of the cutting instrument of the cautery. And be cautious about an incision of the artery in this headache, not one that is old properly.
On the manner of cauterizing in ancient headache.
When you treat a headache, with that which we said from the previous treatment, and that which we said in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not matter for treatment: and you see from the illness that what we said from the first cauterization with medicine, or with cauterization with fire, is not enough, then it is necessary to use a knife cauterization until it whitens. After which mark signs on the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or almost that: and put your hand in one vice, and squeeze it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to avoid the continuation of the mandible, which moves during chewing, lest it be burned on one side or the nerve that moves it, whereby spasms occur.
And let there be care and watchfulness of the flow of blood from the artery that has been severed. For in its cutting there is fear, and especially to he who does not know what he does, and is not studious nor experienced: and abandons the operation with him first of all.
And I shall come with a remembrance of the regimen of the flow of blood from an artery according to its mode, and in the place of this book.
If you see that from illness, the cautery does not suffice for him, and you see the body of the infirm enduring the cautery in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, care for the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer a cautery, which we said in the chapter on extracting an artery with a cautery having two blades. For indeed cauterization is better this way and more effective.
On the mode of cauterization for ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear from cold, and it is treated with decoctions and the rest of the cure that we have said in the division, and the pain does not go away, then cauterize with fire; and this is called a Point, whose shape is this.
Then the points with it after its ignition on the circumference of the whole ear, as it rotates: or on the circumference of both, if pain is simultaneously in both. And elongate yourself with a cautery from the root of the ear a little, after you have marked the places with encaustic; and let the quantity of cautery be ten punctures in every ear, and so forth.
Then take care of the wounds until they are healed.
On the manner of cauterization in a torture.
Chapter VII.
A torture which is cured with cauterization, is nothing but from kinds which happen from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses.
And avoid cauterization of the kind that comes from drying and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this type of earache with leeches and head washes and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the diseased person with three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little lower from its time, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite part of the weak. For softening does not occur unless in a part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cautery in the direct extremity of the upper earlobe below the corner of the head slightly: and at another time: whose length should be according to the length of the finger. And place your hand with the cautery until half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a kind from the knife, whose shape is preceded: however, it is not too refined, as you see: and it ought to be a knife in it of superfluous thickness little.
Then care for the place, with that which preceded it: until it is healed.
On the mode of cauterization in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy has aged, and you have treated it with what we said, and your treatment is not effective, and the sick person does not have fever, then cauterize him with four cautery burns on top of every horn of his head, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, as we said before, and with a cautery on the back of the head, according to what preceded: and the manner of the cautery let it be according to what preceded.
It is also cauterized with a cautery over the opening of the stomach: and this is more ultimate.
Then it is cared for, with that which preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in a drink are given first to the infirm large amounts of hyer and purifying pills for the brain.
Then shave the head of the sick person entirely, and place on the back of his head a plaster of synan described in the treatise on plasters: and place it repeatedly.
This, indeed, is the manner of cautery, and do it according to the same order which I said there.
If therefore it is healed through that, it is good. If not, then make three cauteries on the back of his head, which are descending from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cautery the thickness of a finger.
Then care for cautery, as that which preceded.
If, however, you wish an addition, and the patient is weak and enduring it, then make a cautery in the middle for him. If you want an addition: then cauterize it over two horns.
Then care for him until he heals: let the cautery be olive oil according to the form which has been previously stated.
On the method of cauterization in Paralysis, and softening.
Chapter X.
You must proceed with the purification of the head with shears, and with what we have said.
Then scrape the head of the sick person; afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery over every horn of the head, and with a cautery over the back of it, and with three over the vertebrae of the neck.
If, however, you need to soften the body in illness with many of these things, and he is weak and enduring, and the illness is strong: then burn him with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and the last one with a cautery, until it burns from the skin most of it, and raise your hand. Then care for it until it heals; and so apply the cautery of Albucasis.
On the method of cauterization in Epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, unless his epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary that you cleanse the brain of him first with a pigskin, and with the rest of the care which we have said in the division: when he is greatly ill, or is enduring in the acceptance of medicines.
If it is a boy who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and cleansing chewing are administered to the brain, before that many days with improvement of foods.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in manner: and with another cautery in the back of his head, and over every horn of his head with a cautery. If the patient be strong but enduring, then cauterize him with cautery as I said in treating paralysis and softening of the body over the vertebrae of the neck and vertebrae of the back: and let the cauterizing oil be according to the measure which preceded.
If however the boy is weak, then place a fine cautery, according to this manner.
On the manner of cauterizing in Melancholia.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupt humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize it with cauteries which we said are used for those having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of descending humors, and the body of the sick person is humid, then give him in a drink that will purify his brain, according to what preceded in the division; then shave the head of the sick person, and afterwards make a poultice properly made from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and the weak one sitting square shall be held from every part.
Then apply this ointment. It is better from old sheep butter. And heat him over a fire with temperate measure of heating which the finger can tolerate when it is introduced into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of his head in a circle, and let it go until it cools.
Do this for the sick person once a week, with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making small punctures in it most of all, besides which hold your hand with the cautery; indeed let it smell.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with quality.
Then place upon it a cloth soaked in butter, or chicken fat.
On the way of cauterizing in descending water to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When you are told the beginning of water in the eye by the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and wash the sick person's head with it so that it may cleanse him.
And guard him from all moisture, and make him sit in a bath, fasting for several days.
Then order him to shave his head and cauterize it in the middle of his head. Then cauterize it over the two temples with two cauteries, if there is a beginning of water flow into both eyes at once; or from one side, if there is a beginning of water flow in one eye; and cut off with a cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in the width of the temples; and beware of the flow of blood.
If you see something from that, then immediately cut it away with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with the wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting, and care from the flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the neck, under two bones, with two last produced cauteries.
On the method of cauterization in ancient tears.
When the tears of the eyes are ancient and continuous, and they are above the veins and arteries that are on the head outside, it is verified that this is from the superfluities cold, phlegmatic: then cauterize with the cautery same as I narrated in the beginning of the descending water, the cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries in the neck under the two bones. And if you need to add something, then cauterize it on all sides of the eye carefully, above the eyebrow tip with a small cautery.
On the method of cauterizing in a fistula of the nose.
When you treat this, with that which we said in the division, and the treatment does not help: then hasten, and give to drink three nights of a decoction of rue; then shave his head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with an olive cautery. Then cauterize him with a two-pronged burning iron, above two eyebrows under little hairs.
And guard against the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the cautery of Claudius.
On the method of cauterization in softening the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by pain or moisture: then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries in every part: and let them be lengthened from the two temples: and let the length of every cautery be according to the lengths of the eyebrow: and do not bring your hand with the cautery to the end, but according to the quantity which is burned the third eyelid.
On the manner of cauterizing the eyelid when hairs are inverted and piercing the eye.
Cauterization is done in two ways: either with fire cautery or with a burning medicine cautery.
When using cauterization with fire, command the infirm person before it to shave his hair if he is of those who have it trimmed, until they are lengthened and made equal. If they pierce him at his birth place: then bind his eyes with a piece of cloth, that they may not move until they are born.
When therefore they are born and made equal, then put the head of the sick person in your bosom: then mark above the eyelid of his eyes with a cautery, a mark which is according to the figure of a myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a soaked sponge in the albumen of an egg: or in flaxseed mucilage over the eye.
Then a fire cautery, whose form is this.
Then burn over the figure which you marked out in many lines until the skin surface is burned, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, altogether apparent properly.
And the sign of the health of your work is: that if you see the eyelid already contracting, and hairs being removed at the point of the eye.
Therefore raise your hand then: and let him go for three days.
Then put on top of it a compress with butter until the scab is removed. Then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
If something returns of the hairs after an hour, and the eyelid softens: then repeat the cautery over that place, as you did at first.
If hairs are in the lower part: then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural place: and it should be equal so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is as if you should instruct the sick person to shave off hair until they grow long and equal. Make from cloth a form of myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and from unsoaked lime, one ounce each; then rub them together well, and make it with haste so that it does not cool. Then from the paned out of it onto the parchment which you made like the form of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one eye, or two. And place under the eye a poultice soaked in egg white: and the head of the sick person be in your bosom.
And place your index finger upon the medicine, and press it for a short while. And you shall move it whenever the sick man feels the bite of the medicine; because he finds its bite like fire.
While therefore he persevered in this which he himself invented biting, then dismiss medicine, and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting has quieted, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And consider then, if you see the eyelid elevate, as it elevates with contraction with fire, or with incision, it is well: and if not, then repeat over it from medicine on the place where the medicine does not imprint, and does not darken, until your operation is equal, and the eye contracts.
Then place upon it a cot with butter until the burned skin is eradicated. Then care for it with diaphanic ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you in surgery, that you guard carefully, lest anything from the medicine fall into the eye.
If the eyelid softens after days, and something fights from the hair in the eye, then again apply medicine to that place which softens from the eyelid properly, just as you did at first. Then take care of it, until it heals.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of humans differ in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that, let your consideration be this: and the way of righteousness is not hidden from him who has a study of this art.
On the method of cauterizing in a lacrimal fistula.
When you treat a fistula, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and your treatment is not effective: then, it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Tell the sick person to place their head in your bosom and have a servant hold his head between his hands so that it may not be moved or shaken.
Then place a poultice of infusion in the albuginea of the eye, or in the mucilage of psyllium over its eye; then apply fire cautery, whose form is this.
Let it be concave, like the form of a goose feather quill from one end, with which cautery is made; and if you wish, let it be penetrating to the other end, and if you wish, let it be bent upwards.
However, this is better for your work.
Then express a fistula, if it is open, and remove the pus from it, and dry it up; and if it is not open, then open it, and remove its pus.
Then place a cautery heated very hot on it.
And hold your hand with it for a little while near the cautery from the eye to the part of the nose, so that your hand does not stray or disturb the sick one: and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
If therefore you come in the beginning of your cautery up to the bone, it will be well. And if not: then repeat the cautery once, or twice, if it needs it: and let it alone for three days.
Then place a poultice with butter and take care of it with an ointment that dries until it heals.
If he has passed forty days and it is not healed: then put on top of it a sharp corrosive medicine, until the bone is uncovered; and scrape it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some first said. Pay attention to the location of the fistula, and find it; then put into its fissure a fine bed, that is, a fine cannula, whose form is this. And pour into it the quantity of a drachma of lead melted, and hold your hand with a good retention cane, and do not move the patient at all, so that it does not run, or the melted lead comes to his eye.
And it is necessary that you place over the eye of the infirm a poultice infused in albumen of egg, or in water.
For lead, indeed, burns the place of a fistula, and heals it with miraculous healing.
If the fistula is healed, as we have said from cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer a hole in the nose, and to reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what will come in its proper place for itself.
On the manner of cauterizing in fissures of the lips.
Very often fissures occur in the lip, which are called pili, and especially in the lips of children.
When therefore you care for these fissures, as we said in the division of ailments, and the cure does not help, then with a small knife-shaped cautery, according to this form, fire.
And let its concavity be according to the sharpness of a knife.
Then place it burning quickly into the very fissures until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then care for him with a poultice until it heals.
On the mode of cauterizing in a mouth fistula.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then it makes pus, and it breaks; afterwards it matures, and pus runs, and a fistula is formed: then cure it, and the treatment does not help in it, then it is necessary that fires cauterize according to the quantity which takes into the fistula. Then introduce it burning into the fistula's opening, and hold your hand until the burning iron reaches its depth and end; do this once or twice.
Then take care of him after that, as we have said about the cure up to when he should be cared for.
If therefore the pus is cut away and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place, and remove the corrupted bone according to what comes in its head.
On the method of cauterizing in gums and softened teeth.
When the gums soften because of moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not help: then place the head of the sick person in your bosom.
Then apply the burning cautery, which will come in the shape following this, so that you place the tube over the tooth: and quickly insert the ignited cautery into it: and hold your hand for a short time until the one suffering feels the heat of fire has already reached the root of the tooth.
And lift your hand: then repeat cautery several times, according to what you wish.
Then the sick person shall fill his mouth with salt water and hold it for one hour; and he shall spit it out.
For when a tooth is moved, it is set firmly, and the gums are softened and tightened, and the corrupted humidity is dried.
On the mode of cauterization in toothache.
When pain in the tooth is caused by cold or there is cold within it, or a worm, and healing does not help with medicines; then cauterization is done in the tooth in two ways: either cauterization with butter or cauterization with fire.
The cautery with butter is thus made, take clarified butter and melt it in an iron ladle or pan. Then take a swab and wrap it around the end of the limb. Then immerse it in boiled butter: and place it on the aching tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the virtue of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or a cloth in cold butter, and place it over the aching tooth: and place on top of it burning iron until the fire reaches the bottom of the tooth's cavity.
The cauterization of it with fire is, that you may apply to a tube of air, or a tube of iron. And let there be something of thickness in his body, so that the sharpness of fire does not reach the bone of the infirm.
Then set the cautery to fire, whose form will come: and place it upon that tooth: and hold your hand, until the cautery cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or another day.
And it is necessary in the cautery's application, that the sick person fill his mouth with good broth and hold it for one hour; then he should spit it out.
And this is the form of cautery.
Cauterize with whatever extremity you wish according to what is possible: and this is the form of the Cannula.
On the manner of cauterization in strophuli.
When the strophulae are from phlegm and from cold humidities, and they are not obedient to digestion by medicines, and you wish to hasten their digestion, then a concave cautery fire whose form is this:
Having two open ends so that smoke may exit at one end when cauterizing from the other end: and place it lit upon the abscess once, and again, if needed, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
If the abscess is small: then place cautery according to the size of the abscess.
Then dismiss him for three days and place over it a poultice infused in butter until that which was burned by fire is removed.
Then care for it with toothpaste ointment until the shape of the tube heals.
On the method of cauterization for hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When humidity accumulates above the lung canal, and especially when it is with a cold constitution, then it is necessary that the sick person be evacuated first with medicines of solutions.
Then cauterize it at the root of the throat, in a depressed place: and beware, lest you come with the cautery to the throat, nor into the skin, unless something of it.
Then cauterize him with another cautery at the junction of the neck at its last vertebra; and let the cautery be clamped according to the manner which preceded.
Then care for him as before, until he is healed.
On the mode of cauterization in illnesses of the lungs and cough.
When a cough and lung ailment are due to cold humors, and the patient does not have fever or consumption, and the ailment is old: then cauterize him with two cauteries above the fork in low, soft, hollow places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples: and let the cautery be a tube according to the form which preceded.
And if you wish to cauterize your wound by pricking with a cautery called 'Punctum', whose form precedes in the pricking of ear pains: and let there be points from thirty points up to almost others.
Then take care of him with that which preceded, until he is healed.
And now let there be a cautery having three branches: according to this form. Therefore it should be relieved with it cauterization, when you make with it once three cauteries.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head is dislocated because of humidity and it does not return to its place within an hour after its dislocation, until it has become accustomed to returning, then it is dislocated with a slight movement, which happens as we have already testified, then it must be reduced back into place. Then the sick person is laid on their back, or on their sound side. Then raise the skin that is in the inner Tilici to the upper parts with your left hand fingers: and if the joint is dislocated inwards.
Then with a cauterizing fire he has two instruments. Its shape is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of cauterization will come with four cauteries.
And sometimes cauterization is done with a cautery having three cords, therefore the figure of cauterization then becomes six cauteries: and the cords are according to the subtlety of the thread.
And this is the shape of a cautery having three handles.
And sometimes one is added above this mode, wherefore there are eight cauteries.
Then put on top of the cautery crushed leeks with salt. Then make the injured person lie still so that the limb is not moved for a while until it has strengthened.
And if the dislocation is upward, and this rarely happens, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a single cautery, or with many cauteries by puncturing.
For the joint is strengthened and humidity is removed: and the infirm is healed.
On the manner of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and much moisture occur in the stomach until it is drawn out of its composition, and phlegm multiplies to it, and continuous treatments are applied, and it does not help: then it is necessary that the sick person be laid on his back, and stretch out his legs, and hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery under the ear of the breast the size of one finger with a clauili cautery, and two cauteries below from both sides of one cautery, until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular. And make it extend between the two so that they may not join when they make pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the quantity of two thirds the thickness of the skin.
And let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery which does this cautery be one according to the figure of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking it for him who fears this cauterization; and it is, as signs on the stomach point according to the quantity which you wish with encaustration; then cauterize it with a cauterizing point; then cure it with the cure which preceded until it heals.
On the manner of cauterizing a cold abscess.
When pain occurs in the liver from cold and moisture, or from thick wind, until it leaves its composition by natural discharge of superfluity, and the patient is healed with what we have said, and does not improve: then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back on his neck, and three cauteries with encaustic signs according to this figure and this same quantity below the epigastrium from the hypogastrium, where the elbow of man reaches. And let the space between every cautery be according to the thickness of the finger: and let the cautery be according to the length of the body straight: and do not press your hand with the cautery too much.
Let the quantity that is burned be according to the thickness of the skin, the quantity of half of it not added: and let the sick person stand upon his feet.
If he is not standing, then let him be lying down, who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of a cautery.
And it is possible for you, that you may cauterize these wounds with a knife cautery, when there is subtlety and prudence in the art with you.
And guard yourself that you do not proceed too far in cauterization, and the thickness of the skin of the whole is burned, therefore the whole body is burned, and it comes to the intestines: because the skin there is thin, know this thing.
On the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When an abscess occurs and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in its tunic; then if it is in the flesh of the liver, a pain invades the weak patient, and heaviness without sharpness: and if it is in the tunic of the liver, there is a pain with very vehement sharpness: and you see now, because it has fatigued his doctors with treatment.
Therefore, it is necessary that the sick person lie on his neck. Then the figure of the place of an abscess with cautery; then fires of cauterium which is assimilated to a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one cautery until the whole skin is burned and it reaches the flesh, until all pus comes out; then care for it with treatment of wounds until it heals.
And one should not use this cautery unless the study of medicine is prolonged, and by whose hands these ailments occur with experience many times; then indeed let him dare to perform such an operation.
But in my opinion, it is better to dismiss her.
On the method of cauterization in pleurisy.
The ancients said that a cautery with the roots of asarabacca is used for cold pleurisy in this way. And it is, that you receive from the roots of dried long birthwort, one root longer, which is found in it, and let it be like the thickness of a finger. Then immerse it in oil and set it aflame. Then burn with one cautery in that which is between the continuation of the fork and the neck, and with two small cauteries under a slight slant towards the part which is below the beard.
And with two cauteries also in that which is between the fifth and sixth rib sloping to the rear a little: and one cautery in the middle of the chest, and one above the stomach. And with three cauteries from behind: one where it is between two spatulas: and two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, lower cautery which is between two spatulas.
And you must not grasp your hand with the cautery, but rather it should be on manifest skin smelling.
And some ancients said that there are men who use a cauterio from iron similar to a rod: and they ignite it, and put it inside where is between the ribs, until it comes with it to the abscess itself, and pus emerges: as we said in the case of an abscess of the Liver.
But in this perforation with a cautery there is fear, that either the weak man dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in its place, which has no healing.
Of the mode of cauterizing the spleen. Chapter XXXII.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, as we have said from the treatment in the division of illnesses, and your treatment is not effective, then cautery in it is according to three ways, which are all right.
One of these is to make three cauteries, or four, lining them according to the length of the spleen according to the figure of the liver cauteries, which preceded.
And let there be between every cautery a quantity of thickness of a finger, or a little more or less.
And let the mode of cauterization be as we said in the cauterization of the liver, equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: and let the weak one lie on his back.
And another way of cauterization is: as having a cautery with two handles, which we said in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder: and elevate the skin, which is on the direct spleen, where the elbow of the left arm reaches: and let your elevation be such that you elevate the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall according to the length of the body.
Then introduce two burned cords far into it, until you penetrate the skin from the other side; then withdraw the cautery: thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with a cautery having three handles.
Then care for the cautery after you have allowed it to discharge pus for many days, for it is more effective than anything that has preceded from the cure.
On the manner of cauterization in dropsy.
Cautery does not fall in dropsy, unless it is applied properly.
When you treat Hydropsy with the methods of treatment which we have said in the division, and the cure does not avail, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery over the stomach, and another over the liver, and one over the spleen, and two cauteries behind the back between the vertebrae, and one on the direct chest, and another on the direct stomach: and let the quantity of depth of the cautery be near to the thickness of the skin.
Then release the open cautery so that it may discharge pus for a long time.
And do not remove the weak patient from treatment after cauterization with him: because it is necessary that two intentions be gathered together with him: and he will hasten to him healing with the help of God.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be a clamp: according to what preceded, its shape. And that with which the back is cauterized, should be an olive according to what preceded its shape.
On the manner of cauterizing feet and legs.
When abscesses are treated in a Hydropericardium, and are filled with yellow water: it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and annular; and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it: then raise your hand: and do not repeat it at all.
The water of citron will then boil, and let the cautery be according to this form.
Then make on each of the two legs two cauteries in every leg, and let the cautery be made with the edge of a knife cautery: and let the cautery be made according to the length of the leg, one under the knee, and the other lower than that, about the middle of the leg: and on each hip two cauteries: and dismiss the open cautery without treatment for a long time: so that it will subside from it some water: then cure it with the rest which we have said.
On the manner of cauterization in the treatment of a rupture.
Chapter XXXV.
When the solution of the belly is from cold and humidity until it weakens the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines: and it is cured with modes of cure, and it does not heal: and you see the weak one enduring cautery of exuberant virtue, then cauterize him with a great cautery over his stomach, according to what preceded in the cautery of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four subtle cauteries in the circumference of the navel, with a subtle cautery. And with a cautery above the alcatin above the alhosos large, or two cauteries.
And if you see excessive humidities and the weak tolerating it, then cauterize it with a cautery on the comb, and a cautery on all of that; and perhaps you add two small cauteries near the large stomach.
It is indeed a healing treatment, whose benefit does not fail.
On the manner of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When hemorrhoids in the anus are old, many, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupted humidities, and they are cured with that which we said in the division, and treatment does not help: then cauterize with three cauterizations on the lower spinal bone of the back under the armpit a little triangularly, and the cauterization under the navel as if it were two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is cold, and his food is not digested, and you see his face festering, then cauterize him over the stomach with a large cauterizer, according to what preceded: and with a cauterizer over his spleen, and another over his Spleen, with a caulking cauterizer: and let the open cauterium go for some time: then care for him until he heals.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you cut the artery, then apply the cautery which is similar to a ray of fire. Then introduce the burning (instrument) into the cut wound; and your last hand, until the cauterizing reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows; do this once or twice.
If therefore the abscesses are many, then cauterize each one with a cautery according to what we have narrated. Then care for that, when it is applied with ointment until they are healed.
And if you cauterize him with a large cautery over linen, it is more ultimate in aid.
On the manner of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter XXXVIII.
When the patient does not obey the cutting and operation which we have narrated in its place, and is terrified by it, perhaps he is healed with cauterization.
When therefore it happens to someone that he has a fistula, and it becomes old, pus runs out of it, and corrupt humidities. Therefore it is right that you examine her with a subtle probe. Then learn the quantity of its depth with a probe.
Then use fire cautery, which is like a ray. Then insert yourself ignited into the fistula itself and the quantity in which it entered.
And repeat over it the cautery, until all those corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the quantity of your necessity.
And guard yourself against burning the nerve, if it is there, or the large vein: or if a fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then guard yourself from all these places.
And do not do this, unless there is an opening in a fleshy place: and you consider, because it is not penetrating.
Then care for the place until it heals.
If, however, the place is sealed and the materials are cut away from it, and it remains so for a long time: then you know that it is now completely healed.
And if they do not cut away the material from it, then know that it is penetrating, or there is a decayed opening in its depths, or like one of those: whose recollection will come at its place.
On the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys from cold or from a thick wind, and it is lessened because of this which weakens the patient, then it is necessary to cauterize it over almethen on the kidneys, with a cauterizer over the whole kidney with a cauterio clauili, whose previous description has preceded.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time in the very wound. Therefore will come three lines. Therefore they will be more useful in healing.
On the manner of cauterizing the Bladder.
When weakness and softening occur in the bladder due to cold and humidity, until it can no longer retain weak urine, then cauterize its lower part above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubis begin, and with one cautery from the right side and another from the left; and let the length of this cauterization be according to the quantity of a knuckle; and cauterize it with a lower back cautery, or with two cauteries if you need it; and let the cauterium be closed as before.
On the method of cauterizing the Matrix.
When coldness and humidity occur in the womb and pregnancy is prevented thereby, and her menstrual flow becomes corrupted and delayed, and pain occurs to her at its arrival, then it is necessary that she be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a cautery on the lower part of the back above the loincloth, or with two cauteries: and let the cautery be clamp-shaped.
On the method of cauterizing an ache in a dislocation.
When the mucous humors flow to the Anchae abscess and become the cause of its exit from its place; and the sign of this is that one leg lengthens over the other when they are compared against each other; and the place of dislocation is found empty there.
Therefore it is necessary that you cauterize the diseased part above the wax of its own cautery with a similar circle; after you have marked it with encaustic around the wax, just as it turns around; and so that the wax itself falls in the middle of the circle.
If you do not have this cautery at hand, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive-shaped cautery. And let the depth of the cauterization be according to the quantity of the thickness of all the skin.
Then care for it until it heals.
On the manner of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the groin and the cause is cold and humidity, and the patient is treated with what has been said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and it becomes old: then it is necessary to cleanse the patient from gross humors with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similar ones. Then cauterize it.
And the mode of cauterization in it is according to two modes: either cauterization with medicines that burn, or cauterization with fire.
A cautery with fire is according to many modes.
One of these is to cauterize over the skin of the anus with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make for them a good depth, or a bad one. And let there be a space that is between every cautery of the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be oiled.
Sometimes a cauterization is done in the middle above the head of the fossa itself. Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip joint, one: so that it contains the whole hip.
And burn the thickness of the whole skin.
This is the mode of cautery for sciatica, when the pain adheres to the buttock itself and does not extend to the hip and leg.
If it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cautery irons above the hip, above the place indicated by the sick man where there is pain, and with your cautery on the tail four fingers' width to the left side a little: and let the cautery be a knife.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
If the patient says that the pain extends nearly to the toes of the foot, then cauterize him there where he indicates with a cautery point, three, or four, or more if needed.
And if he indicates pain being under the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with a one-bladed knife cautery.
And be careful in all your cauterizations, that you do not go too far with the cautery so that you burn the nerves, or a large artery, and thus draw through it over the weak ailment evil, or contraction.
And I have indeed seen one and another of those who cauterized above the ankle, and lingered in the cauterization, and the leg was swollen until a tumor followed all the way to the foot, and the whole foot was perforated and corrupted; then there occurred a solution of the abdomen, and death after that.
If pain is in two parts at once, cauterize both according to this method.
And some wise men said in cauterization of the anus, whose cautery this is the mode. Make a probe like a awl from iron, whose diameter is the middle of a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a fingernail, or a little less: and inside that probe let there be a third probe.
Let there be a space between every stitch the width of a finger's knuckle; and let the stitches be open from two parts; and let their height be like a knot, or two knots; and make for them a handle out of iron fitted centrally into the stitches.
Then it is set on fire until it glows red and throws off sparks; then it is placed over the ulcer of the limb of the sick man lying on his healthy side. Therefore cauterize him with three round cautery instruments in one vice.
Then let him be dismissed after three days. Afterward apply plasters with butter: and leave the open wound for many days. Then take care of it with ointment until it heals.
Albucasis says, "This kind of cautery, my sons, we have used little because of the terror of its appearance; and therefore, because we have found few who wait upon it.
Nevertheless it is good for those who suffer, and find with it a place for it.
The cauterium, however, with medicines burning, is so that you make two pouches having a perforated arm, into which descends the hinge of its gate from brass or iron, the length of the wall:  of which the height shall be two knots, or like themselves.
And let there be a space which is between the two quantities the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above: and let them contain themselves against each other, according to this form.
Then place it upon the padding of the bed, the patient lying on his healthy side. And press your hand upon the patch of flesh much. Then pour water heated with a little fire between two circles and keep it for the amount of an hour's time: and let the sick person endure its biting and burning, for he himself has found that the biting is like fire until the biting ceases.
Then elevate your hand with an instrument, and wipe away hot water from the whole wound with sweet water; then let it be left alone for three days.
And place over this butter until the blackness of burning is removed; and let it stand for several days, and pus will flow from it. It is indeed the last resort in healing.
Then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
If pain extends as far as the hip or leg: make for him a statue in that which contains water, according to what you did in ancha equally.
And this is the way of hot water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and unquenched quicklime, each a part, grind them both, and place them in a new pot, whose lower part has a small hole according to the amount that will enter it; and place another pot inside the bottom of the pot; and pour over the alkali and quicklime from sweet water, so that both are submerged by a finger; after which you compress them with your hand good compression, and set aside the pot until the sharp water descends into the lower part of the smaller pot.
Then gather all that water and throw it over another lime stone: and stir until it is renewed.
For it will then be strong and very sharp, which is administered in many operations of medicine, and in cauterization of the remaining limbs. For it produces an operation of fire itself.
And of medicines there are those with which  large wounds are cauterized, just as with the powder of almond and lime mixed with soap, so that both are well mixed.
And Galen indeed narrating retold, of a certain man from antiquity the cure, with which he was cured pain of the hip and sciatic vein: and magnified it to be greatly. And he said that it did not need further treatment, and that it was healed from the one wound, until it returned, because perhaps he himself had entered the bath, brought there, and went out from it already healthy.
And it is, as it should be taken from the green sitaragi: and if it is not found green, take it dry, fresh: and it is to be ordered much with a little fat, and placed over the ache, where pain is, whether in the leg, or in the hip: and let it be applied, and removed after three hours, or for the quantity that the sick man feels sedation of burning. Then introduce him into the bath.
When therefore the body becomes moist, introduce it into the bed. For pain departs, and healing comes.
And know that it is not right for anyone to use a cautery with these medicines unless after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides said that goat dung, when it is cauterized with the vein of Sciatica, helps: and the cautery is made according to this manner. Take wool, and soak it in old oil, and place it over the deep spot which is between the thumb of the foot, and between the ankle bone, and is nearer to the ankle bone.
Then take dry goat dung and ignite it in a fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place him upon wool, and let him be, until it is extinguished. Then again that. Therefore, do not cease doing this until sensation returns through touch up to the end and the pain subsides.
And this mode of cauterization is called cautery Vaccinum.
On the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, either from a fall, or from a blow, or from the evacuation of superfluity, and things similar to these, from the infusion of cold and moist material: and cauterization indeed does not apply except in this single kind, which is made from the infusion of cold material.
Therefore, after evacuation of the patient, with foul pills and similar ones, three lines should be made across the back, where there is pain, according to the width of the affected area, after marking the lines with encaustic, on every line five cauteries, or more according to the quantity that comes from the endurance of the patient and his strength: and cauterization shall be done with a cautery point.
And if you wish, cauterize with three cauteries, or four, with a medial clamp cautery, according to this form.
On the manner of cauterizing an incision in gibbosity.
This illness often happens to young children.
And the sign of its beginning in boys is: that which happens upon him constriction in breathing at elevation, and movement: and you find it in the last vertebra of the back and its knots, which has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When therefore you see that and wish to make it, then cauterize it with a cautery which is circular according to this form.
And let him take the cautery over all part of the vertebra equally: and if you wish, cauterize in the circumference of the vertebra with the cautery points two lines, or three: and let the points be near to each other.
Then take care of the place, until it heals with what we said.
And beware, lest you administer a cautery in the hump, which is formed in the spasm of the nerve.
On the method of cauterization for gout and joint pains.
When pains of the joints are from cold moisture, which is poured into any limb of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is customary for physicians to call that properly Podagra.
When therefore gout is treated for its cold cause with modes of treatment, and the pains are not removed, then cautery will remove them.
And it is, as you cauterize him after evacuation at the juncture of the feet, with many cauteries: and let the cautery be Olivare.
And if you need to put points on the face of the foot, then make with a cautery points. If the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize the area above every knee with three or four cauterizations from all sides, with the same cautery as Claudius.
If more are necessary for you with this cautery, then cauterize it. And do not submerge your hand with the cautery, but rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If, however, pains ascend to the knees and back: then administer what we said from cauterization in its chapter.
If there are pains only in the hands, then prick at points around the focus of pain, such as two lines revolving.
If there remain pains in the fingers, then prick them, above every knot, and above the comb of the hand.
If pains ascend after days to the elbows, or to the shoulders, then cauterize both sides from every part.
And do not discharge a sick person from good regimen, from the taking of medicine. For if a good regimen is followed and phlegm is evacuated, he will be healed with the help of God with this cautery.
On the method of cauterization in ruptures.
When rupture occurs in the groin and intestine or spermatic cord descends to the testicle, and this is beginning to be near, then it is necessary that you order the sick person to abstain from eating on his day. And let him use emollient substances so that stool descends from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and command him to hold his breath until it comes out, or appears the spleen or intestine.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with a cautery under the rupture over the bone of the breast, with a sign whose extremity is similar to half a circle toward the upper part of the body.
Then a fire cauterizing, whose this is the form, until it comes white and throws sparks. Then reduce the intestine, or the rectum to its cavity. Then the assistant places his hand over the place so that the intestine does not protrude; and you have already opened between the legs of the sick person, and placed a board under him, and one serving over his legs, and another over his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery over that mark, with your hand and the standing cautery straight. And hold it until you bring it to the bone; or carry it with a different tool, if you have not brought it together with it at first all the way to the bone.
And carefully observe from the exit of the intestine at the time of your cauterization, so that you do not burn it, and that there may not come through it upon the weak either death or great evil.
And know that when you do not obtain with a cautery an opening of the bone, your operation does not help.
And it is necessary that the cautery for infants be fine, according to their measure.
Then care with the remaining ointment until it heals.
And let the sick person lie on their back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you give him nourishment in accordance with the length of time of his healing, which will soothe his belly so that it does not leave the intestine at the time of defecation and evacuation.
Then when he wants to rise after forty days, then administer a well-made bandage, and let him hold it for another forty days.
And he should avoid labor and overeating of food and drink and loud voices.
For when this regimen is used, it heals with complete healing.
And I shall say the cure of ruptures with an incision in its chapter.
When ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen and are beginning, and you wish that they not increase, then cauterize the rupture of it with a round cautery according to its size: and let that which is burned from then be like one-third of it. Then care for him as we have said: and nothing else shall be added.
And some first said that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it has been marked with encaustic wax, and a line is placed which is across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with a cautery closed.
But a cautery is first easier and better.
On the manner of cauterization in pains due to a fall, or percussion.
Chapter XLVIII.
When it happens in certain limbs by chance, or by blow pain; and that pain perseveres for a long time, and it does not help in it healing with medicines: then it is necessary that it be cauterized with a pointed cautery.
Let the cautery of every member be according to the size of it, and its ability, and its weakness, and its power, and the location of the twisting, and the pain from it.
If therefore it is healed from the first cautery, it is well. If not, then repeat over the same cautery.
Because it is customary for these pains to shift from one limb to the one next to it. Therefore it is necessary that you follow them with a cautery until the sick person is healed.
On the manner of cauterization in leprosy.
Leper sometimes are helped with cautery and great help. And especially the kind of leprosy, which comes from the rotting of phlegm and black bile: when therefore you wish to cauterize it, consider this.
If therefore leprosy is ineipiciens, and you have treated it with what we said in the division, and it has not descended, nor stood; and fear that over the infirm body corruption will encompass the whole complexion of him: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head known, and a second below towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind the neck.
And last your hand with the cautery briefly, until it makes a small impression in its bone, and the crusts are loosened from it, that the emission of thick vapors may be relieved from it, and cauterize also the spleen with the cautery, as has been said before.
If leprosy has already spread over the infirm person and appears manifestly, then it is necessary to cauterize with these cautery instruments, which we have said in the beginning, and cauterize on the end of the nose, and two cauteries on the two cheekbones, and two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one over the hip joints near the base of the tail and one above it, in the very middle: and two over the thighs; namely, over each thigh with one, and two over the knees; one over each knee, and two over the shoulders, and two over the forearms, and two over the tendernesses of his chest: and cauterize him over every joint, from the joints of his hands and feet: and cauterize over every heel of his feet, and knuckles of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are above the heel bone, lest you burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery on the bone of the breastbone, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the rib.
And know that the more you add cautery, it is more helpful, and more efficacious.
And know that the sick person does not find pain in cautery as the healthy do, because his body is already numbed.
And it is necessary that cauteries be of magnitude and size according to members and joints; according to what preceded from the kinds of instruments.
Then care with a cautery from flour of herb with honey, and the rest of the cure, until it heals.
On the manner of cauterizing in a stupor.
When a certain limb is numbed, and it is treated with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and does not heal, then cauterize that numbed limb with cauteries, according to what the size of the limb deserves, or its smallness.
And let your cautery be driven into the thickness of the skin a little. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes it is cauterized to some kind of numbness that happens to the hand and foot, in the shoulder blades of the back at the exit of the nerves that move that limb: and the numbness is removed.
But he should not presume upon it, unless he is wise in the anatomy of the members, and the egress of moving nerves from the body.
Chapter LXI.
When Albaras becomes antiquated and does not agree in it with anything from the ingenuities of medicine: then cauterize upon it itself with a deep cautery for a little while, according to the quantity of thickness of skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat the wound with flour of herbs, and lentils with rose oil, and arnoglossae leaves, and dove's blood, and kingfisher blood: let one part be taken from each: mix all these together, and spread them on cloth, and adhere them to the place until it is healed.
On the manner of cauterizing in cancer.
When a cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery, as it revolves.
The wise men said that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
To me it does not seem right: because I fear that it will become an ulcer: and I have already seen this several times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we have said; or with many cauteries.
On the manner of cauterizing in Adubelati.
When someone has an abscess and it is slow to ripen, either because of the excess pus forming it, or because of the age of the patient, when he is decrepit with little blood, or because of time, and a desire to hasten the ripening of the abscess, then cauterize around it with small cauteries, puncturing many times. Then let it go. For it itself will hasten with maturation.
If, however, you wish to make a perforation with a cautery, then set the cautery on fire, which has this shape.
And lay him in the middle of Abulcati, until he penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be from what follows weak, so that it may lessen the course of purges.
Then care for it until it heals.
On the manner of cauterizing a bad corrosive wound.
Chapter LIII.
Consumption is nothing but corruption in a moving member, and it consumes itself, like fire consumes dry wood.
If therefore you see corrosion in a place which can tolerate cauterization with fire, then cauterize it with fire, much cauterium, small and large curettes, according to what is convenient for the place in which the corrosion is.
Then cauterize it from every part until you eradicate the whole corruption, and nothing of it remains at all.
Then let him be dismissed for three days, and put on the places cauterized sulfur rubbed with oil, until all scabs are eradicated and all corruption is gone.
Then care for him with ointments that generate flesh.
If therefore you see that after three days flesh is born with a healthy birth, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then apply the cautery again over that which remains from the corrupt places.
And sometimes it is treated with a sharp medicine when corroding. For it rises in place of cautery.
Nevertheless, a cautery with fire is quicker healing; and I indeed have already said cauterization of it with sharp medicine in division: therefore receive it there when you need it.
On the method of cauterization in the nails and warts.
Chapter LVIII.
This pain often occurs in the lower parts of the feet; it is a large, thick mass that harms the foot.
And indeed there is a cauterization in these things according to two modes: cauterization with fire, and cauterization with hot water.
As much as it is with fire, the cautery should be like a concave beak of a raven's feather; which is to be made from iron, according to the quantity that it contains nail from every part; and have a fine edge.
Then place it ignited upon a stick. Then roll the hand with a cautery around the nail until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail: and let it go for three days until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply a poultice of crushed willow bark with salt, and leave the poultice on it at night. It will be removed from its roots.
Then care for the place with ointment of flesh generation, until it is healed.
If they are not converted, and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet: then administer to them cauterium with hot water: and it is, as you shall take a tube from copper, or iron, or from the wing of a bird: and place it over a spike, or an altlul.
