Then I opened his mouth and pressed on his tongue: and afterwards I fixed a hook into the abscess; then I cut away part of it from him, and there came out of it only a little blood: therefore the woman's throat was healed, and she immediately began to drink water, and then she took some food.
Therefore I did not cease to cut into that abscess many times over a long period; and an abscess followed in the place where I cut, until it was prolonged too much and with it that.
Therefore, I devised and cauterized an abscess between the throat.
Therefore I stood after the addition; then I walked from the place, and I did not know what God did with it after me.
On the incision of a boil.
Chapter XXXVII.
When catarrh descends to the vulva and forms a pus-filled abscess and is long, then it is called perpendicular. And if it is in the lower part large and round, then it is called a vulva.
When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help: and you see that the hot abscess has calmed down from it, and is subtle: then it is necessary that you cut into it.
And that which from it is gathered round and does not have length to it, and is bloody or dusky in color, or black, and does not have sensation; then it is necessary that a surgeon make an incision of it. There is fear over the weak in that.
Therefore, when you see it according to the measure which I have said, and its length, so that you make the sick person sit facing the sun: and press his tongue with the instrument, of which the foregoing account has been made; then fix the hook in the uvula, and draw it down: and cut it with one of the two instruments which I have said in the incision of the two tonsils.
And it is necessary that you do not cut from it except what is added above the natural term without addition.
If you cut from that more deeply,  you will injure the voice and speech.
Then after the incision, use that which we have narrated concerning the incision of the two tonsils: and take care of it until it heals.
If however the patient fears the incision: then it is necessary that you use ingenuity in cauterization of him without fear and trembling.
And the way of cautery on it is not except with sharp water and it is that you put the head of the sick person into your bosom. Then press down the tongue of him with the instrument that we said. Then take from the water which I told you about in the chapter on cauterization, and mix it with lime that is not extinguished, and put it in this instrument, neither thick nor thin, and fill its cavity with it, whose form is this.
Let the extremity where medicine is placed be concave, like the cavity of a snail's shell.
And place the instrument with medicine on the wound itself: and let the sick person lie on his side so that saliva from his mouth runs inward from the medicine, so that it does not descend into his throat and harm him.
Then hold your hand with medicine. And you will from the first apply it upon the wound with a quantity of half an hour, until you see it already darkened and the inflammation calmed by medicine.
And if you wish to receive a bandage and wrap it over the end of the radius bone, and fill the bandage with medicine, and introduce the radius bone with the bandage into a tube from above, until the bandage adheres to the wound.
Do this many times until you achieve what you desire from the cauterization of the vein. Then let it be left alone: for it hardens and falls off after three or four days.
If you wish to repeat the medicine, repeat it: and after cauterization wipe around the wound with a cloth dipped in butter, and cleanse it with that which is around it from the medicine: and cover it with cold water.
And it is treated externally with compresses, and internally with gargles, until it is healed.
This kind of treatment therefore is more healthful by cutting and farther from fear.
And sometimes a wound is treated even with that which is more subtle than cautery and incision: for it is treated with fumigation, according to this manner. Take a cloth and hyssop and oregano and rue and sage and chamomile and wormwood, and similar herbs: and gather all these, or some of them, in a pot, and let them be submerged with vinegar, and let them boil: and the pot should be lined with clay properly: and there should be a hole in the middle of the pot, over which an instrument is placed hollow according to this manner.
Let it be made from silver or copper, and let the end, in which is the grain, be introduced into the bone of the infirm person until vapor ascends to the tube above the cannula, until the tube becomes much darkened.
Then repeat over it many times until it stops.
And beware, lest you make this cure at the beginning of the arrival of an abscess. Generally he adds this in an abscess: and it ought not to be done unless at the time of the subsidence of its heat.
If this instrument is not present to you, then take a tube and put cork at its end so that the bone of the infirm does not burn; because cork prevents steam from burning the bone; and this is from good care with health.
On the extraction of splinters and bones from the throat.
Chapter XXXVII.
Many times something adheres to the throat, either a fish bone or something else.
Therefore it is necessary that you remove what appears from them above which falls the sight, after pressing the tongue with an instrument near the sun, and it is declared to you what is in the throat.
And that which does not appear to you and is hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make a vomiting weak before food is digested in the stomach. Perhaps indeed the thing joined will emerge through vomiting.
Let the sick person swallow a piece of breadcrumb, or lettuce root, or a mouthful of dry bread; or take a piece of dried marine sponge soft: and bind it with thread, then swallow it. When therefore it comes to the place where the spines or bone are, and it is drawn out, then it issues forth.
If therefore it does not come out with that which we said: then use an instrument of lead according to this form.
Let it be thicker than a radius somewhat, and at the end of it there should be a curvature, so that it may enter its throat with ease; and let itself have its head raised upwards.
And let him beware of touching his epiglottis, so that he does not get a cough, and drive it in with his mouth, or spine, or introduce himself with his own hand.
Truly it is better if the infirm one inserts, that is, because of his knowledge of the place of the thing annexed: and he pushes down or draws his hand with an instrument up, the whole thing according to the quantity which is prepared for him, until it emerges.
On the Extraction of Leeches.
Chapter XXXIX.
When a leech is treated with that which I said in the division from healing with medicines, and it does not help, then consider in the throat of the sick one in front of the sun, or in the sun after pressing his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
If therefore your sight falls upon a leech, remove it with a small hook, or with a thin stick carefully.
If it is not possible with these things: then take a concave tube, and insert it into the throat of the sick person up to near the gullet: then insert into the concavity of the tube iron ignited with fire. Do this many times: and let the sick person abstain from water all day.
Then let him take a full mouthful of cold water, and open his mouth in it: and put his mouth into it, and do not swallow anything from it: and move the water every hour with his hand. For when a leech feels water, it immediately falls.
If it does not come out as we have narrated, then fumigate the sick person with cinders, or with asa and the instrument which I have narrated in the fumigation of the vulva.
Do that many times because it will fall.
And the method of operation in fumigation is, to take a pot, in which are live plums with fire: and let the pot be covered with a cover, in the middle of which there is a hole: and let the extremity of the instrument be placed in that hole.
Then throw in the fumigation, and let the sick person put their mouth at the end of the tube, and close their mouth so that the fumigation does not go out until you know that the fumigation has already reached the bloodsucker. For the leech will immediately fall off.
If it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times.
And let the weak person endure thirst, and eat salty food, and other things, and not drink water.
It is therefore necessary that he go out with this regimen.
And this is the form of the instrument with which bloodsucker is extracted from the throat, when it falls upon it itself.
It is similar to forceps, as you see: unless because it has this curve that goes into the throat. And its extremity is like the beak of a bird called a stork, in which there is the roughness of a file: when it seizes something, it does not let go of it at all.
On the opening of abscesses, and their incision, and care in general.
Chapter XL.
There are many kinds of abscesses, of many modes, according to how their remembrance comes, namely one and one in this book: and they are diverse in the piercing of them, and in the cutting of them from two ways.
Of which one is of the kind of abscesses within itself, and that which it contains from moisture.
And the second method is because of the places where it happens from the body.
Because an abscess occurring in the head is different from an abscess occurring in the anus: and an abscess occurring in a fleshy place is different from an abscess occurring in the joints: and to each of these belongs its own judgment from the operation.
And from abscesses there are some which ought not to be pierced, except after the ripening of the pus within them, and the completion of it: and there are also some which ought to be pierced while they are raw, and do not ripen according to the completion.
Like boils that are near the joints.
Because an abscess when it happens near a joint and is prolonged to be until it rots what is around it, perhaps the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted: therefore it is a closer cause of contraction of that limb.
Or it is an abscess in the main limb: for if you delay its piercing until it matures, it will harm either it or through that member.
If it is near the anus, pierce it immaturely: and let it not be pierced if it is a raw abscess, not completely digested, except if it is near the anus so that it does not rot deeply, and lengthens to the interior of the anus, and becomes a fistula, or becomes at its end what does not heal.
It is necessary for you to know the hour of perforation of an abscess, which has matured according to its course: and it is in the sedation of pain, the recession of fever, and the diminution of redness, and pulse, and the sharpness of the head of the abscess: and other signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same perforation in the lower part of the abscess and the more prominent eminence: and let the perforation be deep in length of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the hands and feet, and places of the arms, and tendons, and nerves, and arteries, and finally in all equal places where there is no reflex.
In those which are reflected, go with a piercing according to that limb.
When a boil is in fleshy places, it is better that you release its opening until its digestion is confirmed, as we have said according to the complement.
For if you pierce it before that, the course of the virus is prolonged from it, and there is much dirt and filth, and perhaps the lips of it and its depth will endure.
And certain abscesses are pierced according to the width of the body as necessity demands; or according to what the limb needs.
And it is necessary that you administer in small abscesses a small perforation, and in large abscesses a wide perforation; or many sections according to the similarity of the size of the abscess.
And they are from abscesses, in which it is necessary that the skin be concaved; and it should be cut when it has already been made like a cloth, and has come to an end, that which has already died: such as what happens in many, that it swells, and with buboes.
And among these are those which are cut with a cutting instrument having three angles. And of these there is one which occurs like a myrtle leaf in figure.
Like an inguinal abscess.
And of these there are those in which a round incision is administered, and a lunar incision: and similar incisions to these.
For that one who does not have a head, such as superficial ulcers and boils, it is necessary that he be pierced with a superficial perforation, or only leveled.
And it is necessary, when an abscess is large and has already collected much pus, and you pierce it, that you do not hurry and extract all the pus in that hour; rather, extract a part of it. Then the pus should be left alone until the next day. Then remove something from the pus again.
Do this many times according to the gradation, until it emerges: especially if he is weak of virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old man decrepit: for the animal spirit is much dissolved from the animal with the emission of humors: and perhaps the weak one dies, and you do not perceive.
Therefore, pay great heed to this chapter.
And after you have perforated it, through which you perforate the abscesses, it is necessary that you cleanse the wound: and consider. If therefore the wound is of a small abscess, or is a flat incision, then administer a lint made from linen, or old cloth. And if it is a large abscess, and there are many fissures of the opening, then it is necessary that you introduce into each fissure liniment, until they reach each other.
And if in an abscess you have cut away a part of the skin, or in the surrounding area scooped it out; then it is necessary that you fill it with old dung, or as when it is covered with cloth, or shaved linen wool without moisture: and bind it until the third day.
Then throw it out, and take care of it with what is necessary from ointment until it heals.
If blood should flow during your operation, then administer cold water and vinegar, after having soaked a cloth in them: and place it over the location of the bleeding many times.
If however the flow of blood persisted, then it is necessary that you administer a regimen and treatment and powders which I have recounted in many places in this our book, and from the division.
If it is in wintertime, and the place of the abscess is among many nerves, then it is necessary that you pour warm pills with wine and oil, and place them over the places.
And if it be in summer, and the places are fleshy: then it is necessary that you place poultices soaked in water, and oil, or him with wine and oil, and the whole thing cold. Until the third day, as we have said, then it is necessary that you loosen the abscess and cleanse it, and administer to it what is fitting for its cure, until it heals.
This is therefore what is necessary from the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses universally.
According to the method of distinction, I have already said about every abscess, how the way is to its cure individually and separately.
Chapter XL I .
On the incision of boils that occur in the scalp.
Small abscesses occur on the scalp skin, and they are of the kind of boils, which contain sacs, like little pouches made from a hen's gizzard.
And their kinds are many.
Of these some are fatty; and of these some contain moisture similar to clay; and of these some contain moisture similar to gruel and porridge: and the like, and of these there are also those which are hard and stony.
And in the cutting of all, and their extraction there is no fear, as long as in their cutting it does not oppose the artery.
And the operation on their incision is that you should explore it with an instrument whose form comes after these, which is called Intromissum, until you know what it contains.
If it contains moisture, then dry it out by cutting it lengthwise with a shallow incision: according to this form.
And begin with a cut from line b to line g. When therefore the moisture is evacuated, then scrape out the cyst which contains that moisture, and do not let anything whatever escape from it.
Many times indeed it returns, if anything remains of it.
Then immerse a sponge in Egyptian ointment, if it is present: and if not, in water and salt: and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day. For it will eat away what remains from the cyst.
Then again pass over the same tumor with the Egyptian knife second and third, and if it does not digest with that, until you are confident that nothing remains of the cyst, then take care of the wound with ointment until it heals.
If it contains a fleshy node, then cut it according to this form, with the incision shaped like a cross: and throw hooks between the edges of the incision, and scrape it from every part: and endeavor your strength in extracting the tunic that contains it.
If an artery opposes you, then do what I will tell you after this.
And similarly do in an abscess, if it is stony, from incision, and cure the same, according to what we said.
And incision over a stony abscess is easier; because there is little blood and moisture. And sometimes there are certain of these abscesses that are in the head in some men, with which there is no moisture at all.
Because I cut into an abscess on the head of an elderly woman and found the abscess like a hard and solid stone, rough, white, which could not be broken; and if someone struck it with something thrown, it would wound that thing.
In other boils that occur on the head, besides those which occur in the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the section of all of them should be a superficial section.
Or place the perforation of them always from the lower part of them, so that the flow of healing may be relieved downward.
Then care for him as is fitting from healing.
On the cutting away of strictures in the neck.
Chapter XLII.
These abscesses often occur in the neck, and under the arms, and in the groin: and sometimes they occur in the rest of the body.
And those things that happen to them in the neck are some one thing and many: and they arise from each other: and every Strophula from them is inside its own tunic, just as it is in nodes and boils of the head, just as we have narrated.
And there are many kinds of these Strophulas. And from these there are stones: and from these there are those that contain moistures: and from these there are malignant ones, which do not obey healing.
In that which therefore you see of good disposition in touch, whose manifest color is near to the skin, and moves to every part, and is not joined with nerves of the neck, nor with guidegi, nor with artery, nor is it deep: it is necessary that you cut it with a superficial section from the upper part to the lower part of the body from line b to line g, and scrape it from every side: and extend the two lips of skin with a hook, or with many hooks, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head, and extract it gradually.
And it is a precaution, so that vein or nerve may not be injured.
And let the spatula not be too sharp: so that it does not add your hand with the incision, or disturb the sick one, and you cut what is not necessary.
If you cut a vein or artery, or if it prevents you from operating, then put crushed zeigee or some powders that stop bleeding into the wound, and bind the wound, and let it be until the sharpness of the abscess has subsided, and the wound has softened: or until it begins to rot.
For blood is severed with a knife, therefore return to your operation until you complete it.
Then with your index finger examine if anything remains of the other small strophulis; therefore, cut them and cleanse them.
If the great vein is in the root of a strangulated hernia, then it is necessary that you do not cut the hernia from its root: rather, it is necessary that you tie it with a doubled strong thread, and let it go until it falls by itself without harm.
Then fill the wound on the belly, which you have already submerged in Egyptian ointment. Then take care of it itself.
If the whole Strophula is cut, then it is necessary to join the two lips of the wound, and itself immediately after you see that there remains no superfluity at all.
If you see that there remains an excess because of the size of the Strophula, then it is necessary to extend [it] to cut its root and remove it; and administer the suture which we said.
And what contains moisture from the Strophuli, perforate it with a superficial perforation: so that the place of its maturity appears to you: and place the perforation below that which follows in the body, as we said.
Then administer after the perforation a liniment with ointment, and similar things, so that it corrodes what remains from the corruption, until when you see the wound already cleansed: then take care of it with an ointment that generates flesh, until it heals.
Chapter XLIII.
On the incision of the epiglottis due to an abscess inside the throat.
The ancients said this incision is in the Epiglottis, and I did not see anyone in our land who has made it: and this is the writing of their words.
In those having a synanchia, it is necessary that the section of the Epiglottis be made; when no help is given by it; because all veins and lung are weak.
In those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or throat, or at both tonsils, when there is no pain in the canal, it is necessary to use the section of the Epiglottis to avoid the destruction which is done from before-mentioned preparation.
Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it must be cut under three or four circles of the epiglottis with a small incision across its width, in that which is between the two circles by the quantity that the section should be in the soft tissue, not in cartilage: and this place is convenient for the section because it is devoid of flesh, and the blood vessels from it are distant.
If the surgeon is timid, then he ought to extend the skin of the throat with a hook. Then he finds the skin until he comes to the channel: he cuts the vessels of blood if he sees anything from them.
Then he cuts the fistula as we have said; and it is signified over the incision of the channel from the phlegm that flows out of it, with that which is broken up, and the cutting away of the voice.
And let the open wound be left for a while.
When therefore the hour is removed in which the foreclosure is feared, gather together the two lips of the skin wound, and sew its own alone without cartilage.
Then administer medicines which cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Says Albucasis. The summary of this discourse which we narrated, is not an exposition, unless they see that some of these abscesses has already opened the throat of the sick person: and the patient has been raised above death, and wishes to be intersected by his breath: They go to cut the epiglottis, so that the sick person may breathe over the place of the wound with some respiration, and be saved from death: and for this reason they ordered the open wound to be left alone until the malice of the illness is consumed, and its malice is three days, and as such: then therefore they ordered it to be sutured and cared for until it is healed.
And that which I saw with my own eyes, is that a maidservant took a knife and put it into her throat, and it struck the part of the windpipe.
And I was called upon to treat him, and I found him moaning, as is the moaning of a dead man.
I therefore examined the wound and found blood that had come out of the wound a little. Therefore I was confused that she had not cut away the vein, nor had guided it; and wind was escaping from the wound.
Therefore I attended to his wound and cared for it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the girl except a hoarseness in her voice; and she returned after days to better disposition of herself.
Therefore I say: that there is no fear in the incision of the epiglottis.
On the incision of a groin hernia.
Chapter XLIV.
This abscess called Hernia gutturis, is a large abscess, according to the color of the body: and it is much in women.
And it is according to two modes: either it is natural or it is accidental.
It is not natural certain talent.
An accident is according to two modes: one of which is like swollen knots. And another method is similar to an abscess which occurs from ligation of the artery. And in this there is fear, and it ought not to be presumed upon with a knife unless in what is small; and you prove it, and investigate it with the probe. If therefore you find it similar to a fatty lump and is not suspended with any veins: then cut it as nodes are cut: and remove it with what it contains from the cyst, if it is in a cyst; and if not, then examine the whole of it. Then care for the place as much as is necessary until it heals.
Chapter XLV.
On cutting open swellings called Nodes.
There are many kinds of nodules, and I have already said all their kinds in the division: and it is necessary that I tell here the difference between a Node and an Fistula: when there is doubt making.
Therefore I say, that when the heat and fever and violent pains have subsided until the boiling of excess is calmed and putrefaction is complete, then indeed the fever and heat subside.
When a knot is present there is no heat, nor fever, nor pain, and it contains them in its own bag called sifachin which corresponds to the color of the body. And its beginning is like a chickpea, and it becomes like a batecha, and it is greater or lesser.
And they are according to two kinds: either fat: or containing moisture. And the colors of humidity are many, according to what I said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of a Node, you must examine it, and inquire into it first with the instrument that is called an Intromissor, according to what will come its form in the chapter that is after this.
And the way to investigate abscesses and all kinds of knots is that you take this instrument and insert it into the moister place which you find in the abscess; and you revolve your fingers with it gradually until you know that the instrument has already pierced the skin. Then your last hand according to the measure of the size of the abscess.
Then withdraw what was inserted, and consider what comes out in its track.
If therefore a running humidity occurs, whatever its color may be; then dry it with a superficial incision, according to what I have said in the rest of the abscesses.
And if humidity does not exit in the place of introduction, then you know that it is fat: therefore, make a cut over it having the form of a cross, according to this form, as I have taught you; and suspend it with hooks, and scrape the skin from every part with ease; and guard the cyst if you can on it, so that you may extract it whole with the knot.
If, however, the bladder bursts during the operation, and it is not possible to remove the whole thing intact, since this happens often, then remove it piece by piece until nothing remains of it.
If anything remains from it, whether a little or a lot, a Node returns according to the most.
If it conquers you, and there remains little from it, then fill the wound at its completion with some sharp corrosive powders; and bind the wound, and place above it what sits pus hot, and care for it with the rest of the cure, until it is healed.
If therefore the knot is large, then sew its two lips together, and take care of it as with that which is incarnate.
If however the pulsating or non-pulsating vein is opposite to you, then hasten and fill the place with crushed zegi, and loosen it for two or three days, until the wound putrefies and the boiling of blood rests; then return to cutting that which remains from the Knot.
Chapter XLVI.
On instruments used for incision and piercing of the mouth.
There are forms of intromittors, and they are of three kinds.
From these there is a great one, and from these there is a medium one, and from these there is a small one.
Let pointed instruments of square ends be made from iron, so that they hasten entry into an abscess.
And these are the forms of Experiences, and no, that is, piercing: and one of them is named beris, that is, piercing: and there are three kinds.
Of these there is a large, and a medium, and a small.
It is necessary that these abscesses, and openings, and fistulas, and buboes be investigated by what is between them from the bones.
And for others are made round, smooth, blunt, like large needles which they insert under the buttocks, from citron, or copper, or iron, or silver.
And better ones are made from citron.
And experience is also made with black lead, which is suitable for experiencing fistulas, whose concavity is reflections, so that they are reflected with their softness with those reflections.
And they are again of three kinds. Because some are long, some medium, and some short, according to the quantity of the width and constriction of it.
The shape of hooks, and there are many kinds.
Because these are simple ones, that is, those which have one care: and they are three kinds as you see, Great, Medium, and Small.
And of these are blind pouches, and there are three kinds.
And of these there are hooks having two curves, and there are three kinds: and of these there are hooks having three curves, and there are three kinds: and all these are necessary in their place.
And these are the shapes of scalpels, with which knots and abscesses are cut and scraped; and there are three kinds: because among them is a large one, a medium one, and a small one.
The ends of those which are cut are sharp, the other ends are not sharp: and they are not put thus, unless that help may be given to them in the scraping of Tumors at the fear of incision of a vein, or nerve: and that the weak may be healed by them, and find somewhat of tranquility from burning as he finds in the scraping of an abscess.
They are made of metal and are similar to a distilling apparatus, with which alcohol is made; and at the wide end there is a point hidden by a spatula; and through it it runs inwards and outwards when you wish, as you see.
The form of splints which are hidden between the fingers at the perforation of an abscess; and the sick do not perceive them; and there are three kinds, large, medium, and small.
Wounds of the winds with which blood flow is cut off; and there are three kinds, large, medium, and small.
Let them be made of copper, or citron, round, of short length, as you see: and let them be fine.
And it is necessary that these kinds of Winds be with you large and small, so that you may cut blood by them with speed when necessity requires, and then when medicine is not present to you.
However, do not use them for cutting blood in every place of the body, and do not use them except in fleshy places: such as the hamstrings of the leg, and hip, and the wounds of the arms, and nipples, and belly, and groin, and the like of these, from fleshy, moist incisions.
And sometimes they make small instruments from these similar to the cortices of a fist, according to their shape: with which blood is cut when it flows from the place of phlebotomy, or at the incision of a vein, or artery: and sometimes they are made round according to this form.
Chapter XLVII.
On the care of the nipples of humans which are like the nipples of women.
Sometimes the nipples of certain men swell during sleep (that is, when they begin to dream) until they resemble the nipples of women, and they remain festering with pus.
He who shuns this, let him cut above the nipples with a lunar section, according to this form from line b to line g. Then flay the entire fatness. Afterwards fill the wound with medicinal plaster. Then gather together the two lips of the wound with suture, and care for it until it is healed.
If the nipple inclines downwards and softens because of its size, as happens to women: then it is necessary that two incisions similar in shape to a crescent moon be made on its two upper sides, each one containing the other at the edges of both, until there is a larger line enclosing the smaller, according to this form from line b. to line g. Afterwards, scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about sutures and powders, which are necessary for healing, until it heals.
If, however, you do not deem it necessary to make an incision of it, because of the restlessness of the sick man, or because of the flow of blood: then it is necessary that you fill the wound with a poultice submerged in corrosive ointment, and leave it, until it corrodes what remains of the fat. Then take care of it until it heals.
On perforating an abscess that occurs under the armpit.
Chapter XLVIII.
These abscesses that occur under the nipple are of the kind of hard boils, which contain cysts, and from these there are those which contain moisture.
Therefore, those which contain humidities, ought to be cut with a lunar section, according to this form, from line b. to line g. When therefore the whole that is in the abscess is evacuated of blood, then fill it with cotto vetri, and dismiss it until the next day.
Then remove the tumor, and treat it with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
If it is an abscess from the type of knots of Strophulus, then cut over it, as we said in the section on cutting over Strophulus equally.
If the wound extends so that it discharges pus, then administer a cautery to it, according to what we have said previously.
Chapter XLVIII.
On the incision of an abscess that occurs because of an artery and vein.
When an artery is torn and the skin above it is sutured, often many times a boil occurs from there, and similarly with veins, so that a boil and swelling occur in them.
And the signs by which it is known that an abscess and inflammation are due to artery and vein are: because when an abscess is due to an artery, it is long, gathered deep in the body: and when you push on the abscess with your fingers, you feel as if there were a scraping sound.
And that which is for the vein, is round on the manifest body.
And a section above this abscess is an error, and especially that which is under the armpits, and groins, and neck, and in many places of the body: and it is very great. Therefore it is necessary that his care be cured with iron, and what from those also is at the extremities, or in the head, it is necessary that it be cured.
Therefore, upon that which is from them through the inflation of the opening of the Artery, make a cut in the skin in length. Then open the incision with hooks, afterwards the Artery: and free it from the tunics, until it is uncovered.
Then insert under it a needle, and make it penetrate to the other side, and bind the Artery with a doubled thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two Arteries which are in the temples.
Then prick the place which is between two ligaments with a lancet, until all the blood that is in it comes out and the abscess is loosened.
Then administer a treatment that produces pus until the ligaments fall away; afterward care for it with suitable ointments until it heals.
If it is an abscess due to the cutting of a vein, then you should hold with your hand as much as possible of the abscess with the skin. Then introduce a needle under the place which you have held with your hand, and make it penetrate: and let there be in it a thread double, until you withdraw it from the other side. Then tie the ligature with the abscess itself with a good ligature; according to what I told you about the ligature of the uterus, from two parts with two ends of thread.
If you fear that the thread being removed will cause trouble, then introduce another needle with a different thread under the entire abscess at the incision; press and tighten your threads in four places.
Then dry up the abscess in its middle until it discharges what is within; then cut away the excess skin and release what was bound from it.
Then place over that little bit which you have submerged in wine and oil. Then administer treatment, which is done with lead and ointment, until it heals.
Chapter L.
On an abscess that occurs from a twisting of the nerves.
Just as an abscess occurs in an artery and vein, so it also occurs in a nerve; which happens to them through percussion, or from excessive labor, and the like: and it is most common in those places of the assistants, or the heel, and in every place where joints move: and it is a serious abscess.
Its color is similar to the rest of the body, and it is found in many positions without pain: and when it is squeezed with force, it feels like a stupor in it, as if weak.
And it is not an abscess collected deep in the body, but it is under the skin, and it moves to every part, and does not go to the anterior parts, nor forward or backward to the posterior parts.
Therefore, what is in the joints from these things, it ought not to be invaded with iron. Perhaps contraction may occur.
In that which is in the head, or on the forehead, cut the skin with a knife. If therefore the abscess is small, then hold it with forceps and cut it away from its root.
And if it is large, then suspend it with a hook, and scrape it; then remove it, and gather the wound together with suture; and care for it until it heals.
Chapter L I.
On cutting an abscess that occurs in the belly.
Certain people experience, many times, in their bellies and in other parts of their bodies, growths which are called Fungalia, because of their similarity to mushrooms.
Their root is slender, and their heads are thick, and their lips are turned inward. And there is a small part among these: and there is a great part that is highly magnified.
And I have indeed seen a man, and in his belly there were two tumors, which were more like mushrooms than other things: there was no difference between them, white, small roots, and their lips were reversed, and they could be found, and moisture ran out of them always.
Therefore, I cut into it, and I found in one side as much as X and VIII ounces, and in the other side as much as VI ounces. And the operation in cutting them is, that you consider then, if the patient is moist and the color is white, moist, and subtle of root: then cut it with a wide spatula, and have cautery in fire present.
For often much blood is expelled during its section: therefore if you are overcome by blood, then cauterize it.
If you see a weak and timid patient afraid of the cut with iron, then take a lead wire properly made and tie it with it to the athleul. Its method is what we said, and release him for two days.
Then add lead to the constriction. Therefore, you should not stop tightening the lead until it is pressed into the drill and cuts off by itself without effort.
If however the root be thick, then there is some fear and trembling in its incision, especially because it is in the belly.
Nevertheless, it is possible to cut its half. Then cauterize it so that it does not return.
Then take care of the wound until it is healed.
And beware lest you presume to cut into that which is dusky in color, with few sensations, and of foul appearance: for this is a cancerous abscess: and I shall come back after this with a remembrance of Cancer.
Chapter LII.
On the treatment of umbilical hernia.
A protrusion of the umbilicus occurs from many causes. Or from fissures which are above the belly: and it goes out of it either the large intestine, or the intestine, according to what happens in the other ruptures. Either from blood that flows from the Vein, or from the Artery, according to what has been said before. Or compressed from windiness in it.
If it is due to a fissure of the skin and discharge of pus: then its color is similar to the color of the body: and it is soft, without pain: and it appears in various locations. And if it is because of the protrusion of the intestine, then its location is, with that which we have narrated, of more diversity. When therefore you press him with your fingers, he is hidden; then he returns, and perhaps there is a sound with him; and it is much magnified at the entrance of the bath, and labor pain.
If it is due to moisture, it is soft, then it is not covered when you press it with your hand, nor is a bandage applied, nor added.
If it is due to blood, then with these signs the abscess appears black from the  incision.
If it is due to flesh born: then it is a grave, large, hard abscess and it takes shape according to the quantity of one.
If it is due to windiness, then its touch is gentle.
And the operation on it is, that you consider then, if the prominence of the navel is because of blood from the Artery, or Vein, or windiness: then it is necessary that you forbid its cure. For in that there is fear and dread, as I have taught you in the chapter, in which I said abscesses because of the artery and vein.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to the intestine or a hernia, then it is necessary for you to instruct the patient to hold his breath and stand upright extended. Then signs with a cauterizing implement around the whole belly button. Then command him to lie down between your hands upon his back. Then around with a wide spatula on the circumference of the umbilicus over the place which you have marked with encaustic. Afterward extend the middle of the abscess upward with a large hook. Then tie him around with a strong thread or silk cord firmly bound: and let the knot of the ligament be well fastened.
Then open the center of the abscess extended above the ligament. If therefore you find it already captured by a ligament: then extract it with the forceps and introduce your index finger into it, and drive the intestine into the interior of the abdomen: and if you find a tumor, then take it with a hook and cut away its excess.
If however, the artery or vein is contrary to you, then wind around it much. Then return to your operation. Take two needles and insert two strong threads into them. And insert two needles into the circle you made around the abscess in the shape of a cross, so that they penetrate.
Then bind the abscess in four places above the needle: and if you wish, remove the needle, and release the place until the extended flesh decays: and falls by itself: or cut it yourself when it becomes soft and decays.
Then care for him with what is necessary from ointment until he heals.
If the prominence of the navel is from flesh or moisture, then it must be scooped out like an abscess, as we said. And you shall draw out blood, or moisture, which you find there.
Then care for it with that which solidifies the place.
Chapter Fifty-Third.
On the treatment of cancer.
We have already said in the division of the kinds of cancer, and how is the way to its cure with medicines: and beware of it when curing it with iron, so that it may not ulcerate: and we have said about cancer generated in the womb, and beware of its cure.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer is in a place where it is possible to eradicate it; such as cancer that is in the nipple, or in the hip, and those similar ones, from members located to remove the whole of it: especially when it is beginning small.
When, however, it becomes old and large, it is not proper that you approach it.
For I was not able to heal anyone from it; nor have I seen anyone before me who has succeeded in doing so.
And the operation in that case, when it is located as we have said, is, as before, and to free the sick person from black bile several times. Then if you find the lancet filled with blood plainly.
Then prepare the weak with preparation, in which it will be spoken of with the operation.
Then throw into the tumor hooks that correspond to it. Afterwards, hollow out the entire thing with a blade, according to examination, until nothing remains of its roots: and let blood flow, and do not cut it quickly, rather express the places, and wipe away the gross blood altogether with your hand, or with whatever instruments are possible there.
If however a thick flow of blood from an incision in an artery or vein troubles you, then cauterize the vein until the blood is stopped. Then care for it as well as the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
On the Treatment of Hydrops.
Chapter LIIII. Now we narrate in the division of kinds of Hydrops, and how the gathering of water is made: and the signs of every kind, and its cure with medicines.
And that which is cured with iron, is only a species of asclisis alone; and it does not approach with iron the kind of tympanitis; nor the kind of hypocarchia entirely; for that one is mortal.
When you have already treated this type of Hydropsis of the tympanum with medicines, and your medicine has not helped, then consider. If weakness has already come upon the sick person, or if there is another infirmity with him besides dropsy: such as if he has a cough, or diarrhea of the belly, and the like: then beware that you do not treat him with iron: because there is fear of this.
If you see a patient with excessive strength and there is only dropsy accompanying him, and he is neither a boy nor an old man, then the mode of operation in him is that you raise the patient standing between your hands, and the assistant behind him expresses his belly with his hand pushing water to the lower part of the chest.
Then take a grooved knife, according to this form. Let there be two pointed parts, long, and acute at the end like a spatula. Nonetheless, let there be something of brevity gradually so that you do not pass through with it at the operation up to the intestines and wound them.
Then consider. If a generation of dropsy is from the part of the intestines, then it is necessary that you lengthen with a cut from the navel to a quantity of three fingers, to the lower direct above the breastbone.
If, however, the generation of dropsy is because of liver illness; then let your section be on the left side from the navel three finger widths.
And if its generation is on account of the spleen, then let a section be made on the right side: and it ought not also to be a section on the side upon which the sick person wants to lie, so that superfluities do not flow to that weak place.
Then pierce the skin completely with an instrument. Then introduce your hand into that incision and lift it with the Spatula between the skin, and scrape, as if you were scraping it: and let the quantity which is scraped be the quantity of a fingernail, or about that much.
Then pierce the skin until the sponge reaches the place of vacuum, and there is a place for water. Then extract it, and insert into the opening an instrument which has this form. And it is like a cannula: it is made of silver, or copper, or brass, soft and smooth: which has a small hole in its lower part, and on its sides are three holes, two on one side, and one on the other side: and its end is cut, according to the manner of cutting a reed, as you see: at the upper end of it there is a ring.
For when the instrument reaches the water, then it descends immediately upon the instrument, therefore it evacuates from the water in an hour a medium quantity.
For if you evacuate from it more than is necessary, perhaps the sick person will die in an hour through dissolution of his animal spirit; or it happens to him that he falls into a swoon which approaches death.
Truly evacuate from it according to the quantity of its power, and according to what dispositions of the sick person signify to you from the pulse's virtue, and from its goodness.
Then remove the instrument and retain the water.
This is because it is held back immediately because of the skin which retains the opening which is above the sifa; about which I have told you, so that you may pierce it according to that manner.
Then on the next day repeat the instrument if you see that the sick person can tolerate it; and also withdraw from the water a small quantity.
Do this for several days without fear, and guard yourself against error until there remains little water left.
If however you fear for the weak one, and release much water from him; then care for him with burial in hot sand, and much sweat in a bath and sun, and let him wait upon thirst. And care for him with drying medicines, until he is healed. And cauterize over the stomach, and liver, and spleen, after the extraction of water: according to what I have narrated in that which precedes.
On the care of infants who are born with their urinary openings not perforated.
Chapter LVII.
When someone is born from the womb of their mother and the head of their offspring is not perforated, or is a stricture, or is not in its proper place.
Therefore, one must help with its perforation immediately when it is born with a spatula finely and delicately, according to this form.
Then put a thin lead rod into the hole, and tie it: and hold it for three or four days.
When therefore he wants to urinate, he should remove it and urinate. Then reduce it.
And if you do not put lead, it is now possible that the urine which flows over the place, will not allow it to close.
He who has a narrow opening is treated with lead, as we have said, for many days until it is widened.
Those who have a hole in a place not their own are harmed. That is because from those who are born, there is an opening at the end of the penis: therefore he cannot urinate forward until he elevates the penis with his hand upward. It is not generated because sperm cannot reach the womb in a straight line, and it is a very foul ailment.
And the mode of operation in this is that the sick person is laid on his back. Then extend the head of the rod with your left hand forcefully, and cut the head of the rod from the place of the penis, with a sharp point or knife; just as you would cut a reed, or something else, so that its middle comes out like the head of the rod: and so that a hole falls in the middle according to what is necessary.
And beware during your operation of blood flow. Many times indeed this occurs. Therefore oppose him with that which cuts off blood, and care for the wound until it is healed.
On Albucasis which things happen in the foreskin and head of the penis, and corruption, blackness, and adherence.
Chapter LXVI.
Many times these things happen to Albucasis on the staff, and there is a lump of foul flesh.
And from it some are malignant and some not malignant.
Therefore, you should not suspend a non-malignant tumor with a fine hook, and cut it off until you have completely removed it. Then place upon it a compress soaked in Egyptian ointment. Then care for it afterward with dyacin ointment until it heals.
If Albather is malignant, of foul color, then it is necessary that you administer cauterium in it after its incision and the excision of it.
If, however, the foreskin of a captive who has not been circumcised is caught, and part of the prepuce is inside, and part outside: then it is necessary to remove the prepuce that is inside first, until it is healed, then care for the part outside; because when you care for both at the same time, the foreskin does not heal but is pierced.
And now also there happens even in the testicles and prepuce blackening and corruption. Therefore, it is necessary for you to hollow out everything that has been blackened and which wants to be corrupted or already is corrupted.
Then a line on top of it after this with honey that is already mixed with flour and the rind of pomegranate seeds, and herb triturate strainer-like.
Then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
If blood flow occurs, then administer cautery with a lunar cautery, according to this form.
Cautery is a remedy for two dispositions at once, namely for the flow of blood, and for a wound when it is corrupted.
If the head of a urinal is worn away and destroyed within an hour, then you should insert into its opening a lead tube so that the patient urinates over it.
In the adhesion of the foreskin with the head of the penis, and this adhesion does not occur unless in the one whose foreskin is healthy, and circumcision is not required on it: and sometimes adhesion occurs because of a wound or abscess: therefore it is necessary that you scrape it with an obtuse Spatula until the ligament is loosened, and the head of the penis is freed from every part.
If it is difficult to distinguish these subtle things, then it is necessary to excise something from the head of the penis and from the prepuce. That is, because when the foreskin is thin, it may be pierced because of its thinness quickly.
Then separate between the prepuce and the head of the penis with a fine linen cloth which has already been moistened in cold water so that they do not stick again.
Then it is treated with wine and a poultice until it solidifies.
Chapter LVII.
On the purification of infants, and the cure of diseases that happen to them by error.
Circumcision is not a solution of continuity, like the rest of the wounds: but since it is from our operation, by our will, and its use is proper to boys, it is necessary that we mark in it a better operation, and a smoother way leading to health.
Therefore I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision in any of their books; because they do not use it in their laws, and it is only what we have acquired through experience.
Which is because I found that most artificers and bloodletters use purification, cutting with a knife, and with forceps: and they use the cautery, and tie with thread, and incision with a nail.
And I indeed have already proven all these methods, and I have not found a better purification with forceps, and binding with thread.
Because in cleansing with a knife, many times the skin escapes. Because the foreskin has two layers of skin: therefore perhaps the upper skin is cut, and the lower tunic remains: therefore it is necessary to make an incision to cut the other, and future pain will result. And with purification which is made through alfecati, that is, finger-tools, which surgeons use, the incision of the extremity of the male member is not carefully made; because perchance it may enter into its foramen.
In the cleansing, however, if a nail possibly comes out, and spoils your operation; and indeed the skin of a boy is short in nature, and very often they are born thus, that they do not need cleansing; and I have already seen this.
The cleansing with forceps and a cord of thread proved good to me, because the forceps are proportionate to the incision; indeed, the sharpness that is above is like the sharpness that is below. When therefore you place your hand, two points are proportioned, and they cut according to the operation one at a time: and a compression is made of similar figure, containing the skin in its entirety from every side, with which no error at all falls.
And the manner of operating is that you make him estimate, especially a boy, if he is one of those who understand briefly, that you do not do anything except tie a thread on his rod and let him go until another day.
Then make him rejoice and be glad in every way possible to you because of that which he receives through his understanding. Then make him stand between your hands, prepared in stature, and not sitting: and keep the forceps hidden in your sleeve, or under your foot, so that the boy sees them not at all, nor anything of the instruments.
Then insert your hand into its shaft, and blow into the skin, and draw it upward until the head of the shaft emerges. Then cleanse it from that which is gathered in it as filth.
Then bind the marked place with a doubled thread. Afterwards bind lower it a little ligament according. Then hold with your index finger and thumb the place of the lower ligament well, and cut between the two ligaments. Then lift the skin upward quickly and remove the head of the splinter. Then let the blood flow gradually (for it is better), and place powder on top: and above the powder, a cloth in which a sponge has been boiled in rose water, shaken with rose oil. Recently good: and release him over himself until another day: and care for him with the rest of the treatment, until he is healed.
The shape of the forceps for cleansing is this.
Let there be two blunt ends, and let them be intersecting: so that a branch of the clavicle does not go out from them; and let the length of two points be like the length of two manubria equally.
An error occurring during purification is this: for perhaps the entire inside of the skin escapes, or a part of it at the incision.
Therefore, it is necessary that you extend it from your hour with your finger before suppuration of the place; and cut it according to equality.
If you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then remove it with a hook, and cut it.
If it should happen that three days have passed and what is under the stick remains inflated, an abscess; then release it until the abscess sits warm, and excoriate it with ease, and cut into it according to how you prepare for it: and beware of the head of the stick. It will not harm him.
Therefore, treat it with that which solidifies a wound from powders, which we have narrated in the treatise on powders: and if it occurs from the skin above measure, and goes out to the upper parts, it does not harm it even so.
Therefore care for it as we have said until it is healed.
Chapter LVIII.
On the extraction of retained urine in the bladder.
Urine retention in the bladder is caused by an obstruction made from stone, or frozen blood, or pus, or flesh born, and similar things of those which we have said of modes of cure in the division.
And if urine does not pass, and you see that its retention is due to a stone which is already in the neck of the bladder; then it is necessary for the sick person to be bent over his knees. Then his feet are laid upon his back, and he extends his belly from the upper part of his back, and he draws in his failing breath as much as possible. Therefore it is necessary when the neck of the bladder is brought to expel the Stone backward: therefore urine is discharged.
If it is not loosened with what we have said, and the matter is violent upon the weak: then it is necessary that you administer its extraction with an instrument which is called a syringe, whose form this is: let it be of silver, and be subtle, soft, concave like the quill of a bird's feather in subtilty of radius, long in similarity to one and a half palm: to which let there be a subtle cannula at its head.
And the mode of exit of Urine through it is, that you take a doubled thread, and tie wool or cotton onto its end, good binding: and introduce the end of the thread into the lower part of the Syringe: and cut with scissors if anything remains from the wool, but introduce it into the tube vigorously, like a pump.
Then smear the syringe with oil, or butter, and egg white: and make the sick person sit on a stool, and insert the catheter into the bladder, and its rod with moist oils, and olive oil, and warm water.
Then introduce a syringe into the rod with ease until it reaches the root of the rod.
Then double it above from the navel region.
Then drive the syringe into it itself until it reaches the bladder and feels that it has arrived at an empty space; and this is not done in this order unless because the passage through which it goes is twisted.
Then extend the thread with wool gradually. Urine will follow wool.
Then withdraw it, and make urine flow through the urinary tract; and repeat the syringe, and do not cease to do this until the bladder is emptied, and the patient finds relief.
On the quality of cleansing the bladder with a clepsydra.
Chapter LXIX.
When an ulcer occurs in the bladder, or blood freezes in it, or pus is constricted in it, and water and medicines are distilled into it; then a tool called a Clepshydra is made, and this is its form.
It is indeed deaf, that is, closed. And in it there are three holes, two on one side, and one on the other side, as you see.
And the concave place, in which that thing is which drives it, let it be according to the quantity that needs it without addition, until when it is drawn with it something, it attracts from humidities: and when it is driven, with it expelled far away: according to what the clepsydra does, which projects naphtha, that is, Greek fire in battles of Mars.
When therefore you wish to throw liquids into a vein, introduce the end of the syringe into the liquid, and draw with it that which drives upwards, for the liquid is drawn into the concavity of the syringe.
Then introduce the end of it into the rod, according to what we have narrated in the syringe. Then drive moisture with it since that moisture reaches the wound immediately so that the weak one feels it.
Form of a fine enema for irrigating the bladder.
Make it of silver or gold: whose head be higher like a small sickle, and underneath a groove where the ligament will fall.
Then take a sheep's bladder, and put in it the moisture with which you wish to irrigate the bladder. Then bind it between two sinuses with a strong ligature and double thread: and heat that moisture for a little while over fire.
Then introduce the extremity of the clysters into the rod, afterwards tighten your hand above the vessel with a decent moisture of constriction, until the sick person feels that that moisture has already arrived at the vessel.
If you do not have a bladder present, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle from it, and pierce it throughout its entire roundness. Then introduce a strong thread into those openings, as they turn. Then gather a circle, as if it were gathered from a rope; after you have put in it what you wish of moist substances, and oils, and waters.
Then bind the same thing to the instrument: and do with it as you did with the bladder from expression with your hand, until moisture comes to the bladder.
Chapter LX.
On the Extraction of Stone.
We have said in the division of the kinds of stone, and its treatment with medicines: and I have said the difference between stone generated in the kidneys, and the bladder, and the signs of the whole: and I have said the stone upon which operation falls with the hand and section: and it is stone generated in the bladder properly: and he who is fixed in the rod: and I am narrating this with manifest exposition and abbreviation.
Therefore I say that a stone generated in the bladder most commonly happens to boys.
And from the signs of this it is, that urine flows out of the bladder similar to water in its fineness: and there appears in it white sand, and the weak man rubs his stick with it, and labors with it, and many times hangs down. Then it is raised and exits with the rectum in many of them.
And it is an easy cure for children, up to the age of fourteen years. And it is difficult in the elderly. In young people, however, it is medium, in that which is between that and that whose stone is larger, the cure is easier: and if small, it is harder to treat.
When we come to treatment, it is first necessary that we cleanse the sick person with a clyster, which will remove all the feces that are in his intestines; for sometimes this prevents the finding of the Stone at the examination.
Then take the patient with his feet, and shake him, and move him to lower: so that the stone may descend to the deep of the bladder, or leap from a height several times.
Then make him sit between your hands, and let his hands be under his hips, so that the whole bladder may slope downwards.
Then examine him and touch him externally.
If therefore you feel the Stone in the space, then hasten immediately with a cut upon it.
If it does not fall under your touch at all, then you must wipe the index finger with oil of the left hand, if the boy is weak: or the middle finger if he is a complete youth: and introduce it into his anus, and inquire for the Stone until it rests under your finger: and turn it gradually towards the neck of the bladder.
Then press upon it with your finger, and drive it outwards toward the place whose section you desire: and order your assistant to press the scrotum with his hand, and order another assistant to extend the testicles with his right hand upwards: and with the other hand, to remove the skin which is under the testicles in the part from the place where the incision is.
Then introduce a spatula cutting, whose form is this. And find it in the space between the anus and testicles, and not in the middle, to the side of the left hip: and let the incision be made above the stone, and your finger be in the anus: and let a transverse section be made, so that the external section is wide, and the internal one narrow, according to the quantity that the egress of the Stone may be no greater.
Perhaps the finger that is in the anus compresses the stone at the point of incision, and it exits without difficulty.
And know that from stone is made which has angles and margins, wherefore its exit is difficult because of this.
And from that it is smooth, like a gland, and round: and an easy exit is made of it.
Therefore, to him who has angles and margins, add to the fissure.
If it does not come out thus, then it is necessary to put the mind over it; or bind it above it with a twisted bandage, whose end be like the moon, which binds upon the stone, and does not escape from it; or that you introduce under it an instrument, of subtle curvature.
If you cannot work above it, then enlarge the hole a little. If something wounds you with blood, cut it away with a saw.
If however there is more than one stone, then drive first the largest one to the mouth of the bladder. Then cut upon it. Then push a little after that; and similarly do if there are more than two.
If it is large, then ignorance is such that one should not cut over it with a large incision. Because it happens to a sick person one of two things, either that he will die or that he has a constant discharge of urine, because the place does not heal at all.
But administer its expulsion until it comes out; or using instruments in its fracture with forceps until you extract it piece by piece.
When therefore you have completed your operation, then fill the wound with frankincense, and aloe, and dragon's blood; and bind it, and place upon it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or rose oil, and cold water: that a hot abscess may sit.
Then place the patient on his back, on his neck, and not untie the ligaments, until the third day. When therefore you have loosened it, embroider the place with water and much oil.
Then treat it with dyafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
If however a hot abscess happens to be added to the wound, and corroded, and similar to these things: as if blood clots in the bladder, and urine is prevented from flowing out of it: and this is known by the emission of blood with the urine. Therefore introduce your finger into the wound and withdraw blood from it. For if it remains, it provokes the corruption of the bladder and its putrefaction.
Then wash the wound with vinegar and water and salt: and apply to it of every kind what is fitting from healing, until it heals.
And it is necessary in the hours of healing the whole, that you bind two hams, and aggregates, because of medicines which are put upon the place.
If the stone is small and is in the ureter, and it is fixed there, and prevents the outflow of urine: then cure it with what I have told you before you reach the section. For many times indeed you will be excused from incision by this cure, for I have now proven that.
And it is, that you receive a perforator from iron steel, whose this form is, of triangular extremity, acute, fixed in wood.
Then take a thread, and tie it with a stick under a stone so that it does not return to the wound.
Then introduce the piercing iron into the rod with ease, until it reaches the stone; and revolve the perforator with your hand in the stone gradually; and try the perforation of it, until you make it penetrate from the other side.
Urine, however, is completely passed at once.
Then press your hand upon that which remains from the stone on the outer part of the virga. He himself breaks and comes out with urine, and the sick one is healed.
If this treatment is not prepared for you, because of something that prevents it: then tie a thread under the stone, and another thread above the stone. Then dry over a stone in the very staff between two ligatures. Then remove it. Afterwards, dissolve the ligament, and cleanse the congealed blood which is formed in the wound.
And it is not necessary to put a thread under the stone, except that it may not return to the vessel; and another bandage from above, except that when the thread is released after the removal of the stone, the skin may return to its place, and cover the wound: and for this reason it is necessary for you, when you tie the upper thread, to elevate the skin upward, so that it may return to its place, and cover the wound, as we have said.
Chapter LX I.
On the Extraction of Women's Stones.
Stone is produced in women in small amounts.
If however it happens to anyone of these stones, then healing is difficult, and it is forbidden because of many ways.
One of these things is: that a woman may be a virgin.
And the second reason is that you will not find a woman who will reveal herself to a doctor when she is chaste, or from those who have husbands.
The third is because you do not find a woman well-knowing this art, especially the operation with the hand.
And the fourth is distance from the place of the stone: wherefore there needs a deep incision, and in this there is fear.
If necessity compels you to this, then it is necessary to take a female physician who knows well: and few are found.
If you wish to do this first, then seek out a chaste and skilled physician and present the woman to an experienced midwife or one who is proficient in this art. Have her examined, especially by the stone that I have instructed you about in my inquiry.
First of all, it is necessary to see if the woman is a virgin; then it is necessary for him to insert his finger into her anus and seek out the stone.
If therefore he finds it, he should constrict it under his finger, and then order the midwife to insert her finger into the womb of the feeble one, and inquire about the stone, after she has placed her left hand over the vulva and compresses it with a good pressure.
If therefore he finds the stone, then it is necessary that he gradually moves it from the opening of the bladder to the lower parts with the utmost of his skill, until he comes with it to the root of the hip.
Then he cuts above it at the opposition of the middle of the thigh at the root of the hip, from whichever part it is prepared, and feels for the stone in that part: and his finger shall not be moved from the stone, pressing beneath it: and let the incision be small at first. Then he inserts a ray above that incision.
Then he inserts a ray above that incision. If therefore he feels the stone, then he adds into the section according to the quantity proportionate which stone goes forth from it.
And you should know that there are many kinds of stones. From these things it is small and large, gentle and rough, long, and round having branches.
Therefore know its kind, as it shall be shown to you by this above what you see.
If blood overcomes you, then add crushed zegel to the place and hold it for an hour until the blood is stopped.
Then return to your operation until the stone emerges; and do, that you prepare with you from instruments, which I said in the extraction of the stone in men, that you may help through these in your operation.
If blood flow overcomes you, and you know that the expulsion of blood is from an artery which has been cut: then place powder over the place, and bind it with a strip of cloth properly: and do not move it: and release the stone, and do not extract it. Perhaps the weak woman will die. Then care for the wound.
When therefore the sharpness of the blood subsides after days, and the place decays, then return to your operation until the stone emerges.
Chapter LXII.
On the incision for an aquatic hernia.
The spermatic cord is not watery, but a collection of moisture in the white sifac, which is under the skin containing the testicle sac: and it is called sifac.
And sometimes it is in the fold of skin that nature has prepared for him in part of the scrotum, until it is thought to be: which is another testicle, and it is the skin of the testicle between the white tissue, which we have said: and this is not made except rarely.
And indeed the generation of this branch is from weakness that happens to the testicles: therefore this matter is poured out to them. And sometimes it happens from a blow to the testicles.
And this humidity has many colors. Either its color is sloping toward yellowness, or it is blood-red, or it is foul, black, or it is watery white, and this is the most [common].
And the signs by which it is known where the collection of water is, are these. If it is in the white scar that we have said, then the abscess is round to a short length like the figure of an ear: and the testicle does not appear, because moisture contains it from every part.
And if there is moisture in its own cloth, then an abscess is round with a part of the egg, and therefore man thinks that it is another egg.
And if humidity is between the skin of the testicles and the white tunic, then it falls under sensation.
When therefore you wish to know the knowledge of color and humidity, then experiment with the color of humidity in an abscess when a square is inserted, whose form preceded. Therefore, according to what emerges from the trace of Intro mission, judge that which is between them.
When we come to treatment with iron, then it is necessary that you order the sick person to be bled if possible and see his body full.
Then he is laid on his back upon a slightly raised object, and many cloths are placed underneath him.
Then sit you on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on his right, who shall extend his rod to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles, and to the part above the navel.
Then take a broad spatula, and cut the skin of the testicles from the middle along its length, as far as near the pubic bone: and let the incision be made according to the straight line equidistant which divides the skin of the testicles, until it reaches the white surface enclosing them: and scrape this and observe, or rather beware that you do not sever it: and let your scraping be on that side which hangs with the egg more: and carefully examine with the scraping as much as is possible to you.
Then perforate the full syringe with water by a wide perforation, and draw out all the water.
Then separate between the two lips of the incision with hooks, and extend the knife upward, and do not touch the skin containing the testicles: and cut the knife however you are able to cut it, either in its entirety or in parts, especially its subtle side. For if you do not carefully examine it, there is no security in its incision, but water will return.
If however, it proceeds omentum exterior from its own cutting at the hour of your operation: then when you have completed the section of the siphun (a surgical instrument), reduce it. Then gather together the two lips of the skin of the testicles with a suture.
Then care for it as you would other wounds until it heals.
If you find a corrupted egg from another blackness, then it is necessary that you bind vessels which are suspended, fearing the flow of blood.
Then cut away the testicle with its suspensory ligament, and draw out the egg: afterward care for it as we have said.
If water is gathered into two parts, then you shall know that there are two branches: therefore dry the other part according to what you have done in the other equally.
And if it seems to you that there should be one operation, then do so; afterwards remove the blood. And introduce into the incisions wool immersed in oil, or in rose oil: and put before this wool another which you have immersed in wine and oil, and spread it over the two testicles, and the marvel of the belly: and put above double cloths, and they are bolsters: and tie them above with a bandage that is having six according to this form.
Then take two cloths and stitch them together and fill them with a carminative powder, according to this model: and make the ends which are pressed from wool or wet wool: and bind them together with the band around the loincloth: and one end shall receive over the anus up to the back, and the second shall receive to the breast side: and two ends above the two lower hips, and two other ends above the two groins, and gather the whole band around the loincloth.
And sometimes this scrotum is treated artificially with a cautery at the place of the incision with iron; and it is, that you take a thin knife-shaped cautery, and cut with it the skin of the testicles; and it is ignited, according to what we have narrated: until when it reveals the white sifac containing water; then take the cautery, according to this form.
It is similar to the Greek letter.
Then pierce it with that and ignite it until all moisture has emerged.
Then extend a knife with hooks, and scrape with a fine cautery lit, and cut into it as much as possible until you have removed the whole of it.
And beware from egg, lest fire touch it.
And know that this operation is healthier and farther from bleeding, and better than the operation with cutting.
If, however, it causes you opposition at the time of incision or cauterization, a hot abscess, or bleeding, or something else: then it is necessary that you cure what opposes you from it with the care which is fitting for it, according to what was said before.
If however the sick person is fearful and does not wait for this operation because of its horror: then administer the perforation according to what I tell you: and it is.
When it is made certain to you by what we have said about the meanings, that a branch is watery: then it is necessary that you make the sick person sit upon an elevated seat.
Then pierce the abscess in its lower part with a wide spatula: and place the perforation according to the length of the body, and let the opening be wide until water runs through entirely.
Then place a pad over the injured spot, and bind it, and allow it to drain the remaining water; then care for it until the wound heals.
If however the contrariety is to the exit of water at the hour when you pierce it; and it is not otherwise, because the white panniculus makes contrariety in the opening of the wound, and prevents the exit of water: then it is necessary that you insert a feather into the wound, or an instrument with which water from hydrops is extracted, whose form precedes: or add in the operation of the wound a little.
And know that water returns and is gathered after six months, or thereabouts. When therefore it is gathered together, then let it be closed in the same manner, and the patient will pass his days.
Chapter LXIII.
On the treatment of fleshy branches.
Know that in cutting above this branch, fear can lead to harm in many conditions. Therefore it seems to me his dismissal from there is salutary.
And I remember the operation upon it, and the appearance of the abscess.
I say therefore that abscesses frequently occur in bodies, of which some are composed of testicles: and this comes from many causes, namely.
Either from excess of acute or sharp which flows down to the testicles. Or by percussion.
